A server might choose not to send an initial representation, other than
the list of alternatives, and thereby indicate that reactive negotiation
by the user agent is preferred. For example, the alternatives listed in
responses with the [300 (Multiple Choices)](#status.300){.xref} and [406
(Not Acceptable)](#status.406){.xref} status codes include information
about available representations so that the user or user agent can react
by making a selection.[¶](#section-12.2-3){.pilcrow}

Reactive negotiation is advantageous when the response would vary over
commonly used dimensions (such as type, language, or encoding), when the
origin server is unable to determine a user agent\'s capabilities from
examining the request, and generally when public caches are used to
distribute server load and reduce network
usage.[¶](#section-12.2-4){.pilcrow}

Reactive negotiation suffers from the disadvantages of transmitting a
list of alternatives to the user agent, which degrades user-perceived
latency if transmitted in the header section, and needing a second
request to obtain an alternate representation. Furthermore, this
specification does not define a mechanism for supporting automatic
selection, though it does not prevent such a mechanism from being
developed.[¶](#section-12.2-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#request.content.negotiation}
::: {#section-12.3 .section}
### [12.3.](#section-12.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Request Content Negotiation](#name-request-content-negotiation){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-request-content-negotiation}

When content negotiation preferences are sent in a server\'s response,
the listed preferences are called \"request content negotiation\"
because they intend to influence selection of an appropriate content for
subsequent requests to that resource. For example, the
[Accept](#field.accept){.xref} ([Section 12.5.1](#field.accept){.xref})
and [Accept-Encoding](#field.accept-encoding){.xref} ([Section
12.5.3](#field.accept-encoding){.xref}) header fields can be sent in a
response to indicate preferred media types and content codings for
subsequent requests to that resource.[¶](#section-12.3-1){.pilcrow}

Similarly, [Section
3.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc5789#section-3.1){.relref} of
\[[RFC5789](#RFC5789){.xref}\] defines the \"Accept-Patch\" response
header field, which allows discovery of which content types are accepted
in PATCH requests.[¶](#section-12.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#conneg.features}
::: {#section-12.4 .section}
### [12.4.](#section-12.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Content Negotiation Field Features](#name-content-negotiation-field-f){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-content-negotiation-field-f}

::: {#conneg.absent}
::: {#section-12.4.1 .section}
#### [12.4.1.](#section-12.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Absence](#name-absence){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-absence}

For each of the content negotiation fields, a request that does not
contain the field implies that the sender has no preference on that
dimension of negotiation.[¶](#section-12.4.1-1){.pilcrow}

If a content negotiation header field is present in a request and none
of the available representations for the response can be considered
acceptable according to it, the origin server can either honor the
header field by sending a [406 (Not Acceptable)](#status.406){.xref}
response or disregard the header field by treating the response as if it
is not subject to content negotiation for that request header field.
This does not imply, however, that the client will be able to use the
representation.[¶](#section-12.4.1-2){.pilcrow}

**Note:** A user agent sending these header fields makes it easier for a
server to identify an individual by virtue of the user agent\'s request
characteristics ([Section
17.13](#fingerprinting){.xref}).[¶](#section-12.4.1-3.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#quality.values}
::: {#section-12.4.2 .section}
#### [12.4.2.](#section-12.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Quality Values](#name-quality-values){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-quality-values}

The content negotiation fields defined by this specification use a
common parameter, named \"q\" (case-insensitive), to assign a relative
\"weight\" to the preference for that associated kind of content. This
weight is referred to as a \"quality value\" (or \"qvalue\") because the
same parameter name is often used within server configurations to assign
a weight to the relative quality of the various representations that can
be selected for a resource.[¶](#section-12.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

The weight is normalized to a real number in the range 0 through 1,
where 0.001 is the least preferred and 1 is the most preferred; a value
of 0 means \"not acceptable\". If no \"q\" parameter is present, the
default weight is 1.[¶](#section-12.4.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-weight-309 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-qvalue-310 .iref}

::: {#section-12.4.2-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  weight = OWS ";" OWS "q=" qvalue
  qvalue = ( "0" [ "." 0*3DIGIT ] )
         / ( "1" [ "." 0*3("0") ] )
```

[¶](#section-12.4.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::

A sender of qvalue [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} generate more than three digits
after the decimal point. User configuration of these values ought to be
limited in the same fashion.[¶](#section-12.4.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#wildcard.values}
::: {#section-12.4.3 .section}
#### [12.4.3.](#section-12.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Wildcard Values](#name-wildcard-values){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-wildcard-values}

Most of these header fields, where indicated, define a wildcard value
(\"\*\") to select unspecified values. If no wildcard is present, values
that are not explicitly mentioned in the field are considered
unacceptable. Within [Vary](#field.vary){.xref}, the wildcard value
means that the variance is unlimited.[¶](#section-12.4.3-1){.pilcrow}

**Note:** In practice, using wildcards in content negotiation has
limited practical value because it is seldom useful to say, for example,
\"I prefer image/\* more or less than (some other specific value)\". By
sending Accept: \*/\*;q=0, clients can explicitly request a [406 (Not
Acceptable)](#status.406){.xref} response if a more preferred format is
not available, but they still need to be able to handle a different
response since the server is allowed to ignore their
preference.[¶](#section-12.4.3-2.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#conneg.fields}
::: {#section-12.5 .section}
### [12.5.](#section-12.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Content Negotiation Fields](#name-content-negotiation-fields){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-content-negotiation-fields}

::: {#field.accept}
::: {#section-12.5.1 .section}
#### [12.5.1.](#section-12.5.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Accept](#name-accept){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-accept}

[]{#iref-fields-accept-311 .iref} []{#iref-header-fields-accept-312
.iref} []{#iref-accept-header-field-313 .iref}

The \"Accept\" header field can be used by user agents to specify their
preferences regarding response media types. For example, Accept header
fields can be used to indicate that the request is specifically limited
to a small set of desired types, as in the case of a request for an
in-line image.[¶](#section-12.5.1-1){.pilcrow}

When sent by a server in a response, Accept provides information about
which content types are preferred in the content of a subsequent request
to the same resource.[¶](#section-12.5.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-accept-314 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-media-range-315
.iref}

::: {#section-12.5.1-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Accept = #( media-range [ weight ] )

  media-range    = ( "*/*"
                     / ( type "/" "*" )
                     / ( type "/" subtype )
                   ) parameters
```

[¶](#section-12.5.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::

The asterisk \"\*\" character is used to group media types into ranges,
with \"\*/\*\" indicating all media types and \"type/\*\" indicating all
subtypes of that type. The media-range can include media type parameters
that are applicable to that range.[¶](#section-12.5.1-4){.pilcrow}

Each media-range might be followed by optional applicable media type
parameters (e.g., [charset](#charset){.xref}), followed by an optional
\"q\" parameter for indicating a relative weight ([Section
12.4.2](#quality.values){.xref}).[¶](#section-12.5.1-5){.pilcrow}

Previous specifications allowed additional extension parameters to
appear after the weight parameter. The accept extension grammar
(accept-params, accept-ext) has been removed because it had a
complicated definition, was not being used in practice, and is more
easily deployed through new header fields. Senders using weights
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} send \"q\" last (after all media-range parameters).
Recipients [SHOULD]{.bcp14} process any parameter named \"q\" as weight,
regardless of parameter ordering.[¶](#section-12.5.1-6){.pilcrow}

**Note:** Use of the \"q\" parameter name to control content negotiation
would interfere with any media type parameter having the same name.
Hence, the media type registry disallows parameters named
\"q\".[¶](#section-12.5.1-7.1){.pilcrow}

The example[¶](#section-12.5.1-8){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.1-9}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept: audio/*; q=0.2, audio/basic
```

[¶](#section-12.5.1-9){.pilcrow}
:::

is interpreted as \"I prefer audio/basic, but send me any audio type if
it is the best available after an 80% markdown in
quality\".[¶](#section-12.5.1-10){.pilcrow}

A more elaborate example is[¶](#section-12.5.1-11){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.1-12}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept: text/plain; q=0.5, text/html,
       text/x-dvi; q=0.8, text/x-c
```

[¶](#section-12.5.1-12){.pilcrow}
:::

Verbally, this would be interpreted as \"text/html and text/x-c are the
equally preferred media types, but if they do not exist, then send the
text/x-dvi representation, and if that does not exist, send the
text/plain representation\".[¶](#section-12.5.1-13){.pilcrow}

Media ranges can be overridden by more specific media ranges or specific
media types. If more than one media range applies to a given type, the
most specific reference has precedence. For
example,[¶](#section-12.5.1-14){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.1-15}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept: text/*, text/plain, text/plain;format=flowed, */*
```

[¶](#section-12.5.1-15){.pilcrow}
:::

have the following precedence:[¶](#section-12.5.1-16){.pilcrow}

1.  [text/plain;format=flowed[¶](#section-12.5.1-17.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.1-17.1}
2.  [text/plain[¶](#section-12.5.1-17.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.1-17.2}
3.  [text/\*[¶](#section-12.5.1-17.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.1-17.3}
4.  [\*/\*[¶](#section-12.5.1-17.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.1-17.4}

The media type quality factor associated with a given type is determined
by finding the media range with the highest precedence that matches the
type. For example,[¶](#section-12.5.1-18){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.1-19}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept: text/*;q=0.3, text/plain;q=0.7, text/plain;format=flowed,
       text/plain;format=fixed;q=0.4, */*;q=0.5
```

[¶](#section-12.5.1-19){.pilcrow}
:::

would cause the following values to be
associated:[¶](#section-12.5.1-20){.pilcrow}

  Media Type                 Quality Value
  -------------------------- ---------------
  text/plain;format=flowed   1
  text/plain                 0.7
  text/html                  0.3
  image/jpeg                 0.5
  text/plain;format=fixed    0.4
  text/html;level=3          0.7

  : [Table 5](#table-5){.selfRef}

**Note:** A user agent might be provided with a default set of quality
values for certain media ranges. However, unless the user agent is a
closed system that cannot interact with other rendering agents, this
default set ought to be configurable by the
user.[¶](#section-12.5.1-22.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.accept-charset}
::: {#section-12.5.2 .section}
#### [12.5.2.](#section-12.5.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Accept-Charset](#name-accept-charset){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-accept-charset}

[]{#iref-fields-accept-charset-316 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-accept-charse .iref}
[]{#iref-accept-charset-header-field .iref}

The \"Accept-Charset\" header field can be sent by a user agent to
indicate its preferences for charsets in textual response content. For
example, this field allows user agents capable of understanding more
comprehensive or special-purpose charsets to signal that capability to
an origin server that is capable of representing information in those
charsets.[¶](#section-12.5.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-accept-charset-319 .iref}

::: {#section-12.5.2-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Accept-Charset = #( ( token / "*" ) [ weight ] )
```

[¶](#section-12.5.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::

Charset names are defined in [Section 8.3.2](#charset){.xref}. A user
agent [MAY]{.bcp14} associate a quality value with each charset to
indicate the user\'s relative preference for that charset, as defined in
[Section 12.4.2](#quality.values){.xref}. An example
is[¶](#section-12.5.2-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.2-4}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept-Charset: iso-8859-5, unicode-1-1;q=0.8
```

[¶](#section-12.5.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::

The special value \"\*\", if present in the Accept-Charset header field,
matches every charset that is not mentioned elsewhere in the
field.[¶](#section-12.5.2-5){.pilcrow}

**Note:** Accept-Charset is deprecated because UTF-8 has become nearly
ubiquitous and sending a detailed list of user-preferred charsets wastes
bandwidth, increases latency, and makes passive fingerprinting far too
easy ([Section 17.13](#fingerprinting){.xref}). Most general-purpose
user agents do not send Accept-Charset unless specifically configured to
do so.[¶](#section-12.5.2-6.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.accept-encoding}
::: {#section-12.5.3 .section}
#### [12.5.3.](#section-12.5.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Accept-Encoding](#name-accept-encoding){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-accept-encoding}

[]{#iref-fields-accept-encoding-320 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-accept-encodi .iref}
[]{#iref-accept-encoding-header-fiel .iref}

The \"Accept-Encoding\" header field can be used to indicate preferences
regarding the use of content codings ([Section
8.4.1](#content.codings){.xref}).[¶](#section-12.5.3-1){.pilcrow}

When sent by a user agent in a request, Accept-Encoding indicates the
content codings acceptable in a
response.[¶](#section-12.5.3-2){.pilcrow}

When sent by a server in a response, Accept-Encoding provides
information about which content codings are preferred in the content of
a subsequent request to the same
resource.[¶](#section-12.5.3-3){.pilcrow}

An \"identity\" token is used as a synonym for \"no encoding\" in order
to communicate when no encoding is
preferred.[¶](#section-12.5.3-4){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-accept-encoding-323 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-codings-324
.iref}

::: {#section-12.5.3-5}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Accept-Encoding  = #( codings [ weight ] )
  codings          = content-coding / "identity" / "*"
```

[¶](#section-12.5.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::

Each codings value [MAY]{.bcp14} be given an associated quality value
(weight) representing the preference for that encoding, as defined in
[Section 12.4.2](#quality.values){.xref}. The asterisk \"\*\" symbol in
an Accept-Encoding field matches any available content coding not
explicitly listed in the field.[¶](#section-12.5.3-6){.pilcrow}

Examples:[¶](#section-12.5.3-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.3-8}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept-Encoding: compress, gzip
Accept-Encoding:
Accept-Encoding: *
Accept-Encoding: compress;q=0.5, gzip;q=1.0
Accept-Encoding: gzip;q=1.0, identity; q=0.5, *;q=0
```

[¶](#section-12.5.3-8){.pilcrow}
:::

A server tests whether a content coding for a given representation is
acceptable using these rules:[¶](#section-12.5.3-9){.pilcrow}

1.  [If no Accept-Encoding header field is in the request, any content
    coding is considered acceptable by the user
    agent.[¶](#section-12.5.3-10.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.3-10.1}
2.  [If the representation has no content coding, then it is acceptable
    by default unless specifically excluded by the Accept-Encoding
    header field stating either \"identity;q=0\" or \"\*;q=0\" without a
    more specific entry for
    \"identity\".[¶](#section-12.5.3-10.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.3-10.2}
3.  [If the representation\'s content coding is one of the content
    codings listed in the Accept-Encoding field value, then it is
    acceptable unless it is accompanied by a qvalue of 0. (As defined in
    [Section 12.4.2](#quality.values){.xref}, a qvalue of 0 means \"not
    acceptable\".)[¶](#section-12.5.3-10.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-12.5.3-10.3}

A representation could be encoded with multiple content codings.
However, most content codings are alternative ways to accomplish the
same purpose (e.g., data compression). When selecting between multiple
content codings that have the same purpose, the acceptable content
coding with the highest non-zero qvalue is
preferred.[¶](#section-12.5.3-11){.pilcrow}

An Accept-Encoding header field with a field value that is empty implies
that the user agent does not want any content coding in response. If a
non-empty Accept-Encoding header field is present in a request and none
of the available representations for the response have a content coding
that is listed as acceptable, the origin server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a
response without any content coding unless the identity coding is
indicated as unacceptable.[¶](#section-12.5.3-12){.pilcrow}

When the Accept-Encoding header field is present in a response, it
indicates what content codings the resource was willing to accept in the
associated request. The field value is evaluated the same way as in a
request.[¶](#section-12.5.3-13){.pilcrow}

Note that this information is specific to the associated request; the
set of supported encodings might be different for other resources on the
same server and could change over time or depend on other aspects of the
request (such as the request method).[¶](#section-12.5.3-14){.pilcrow}

Servers that fail a request due to an unsupported content coding ought
to respond with a [415 (Unsupported Media Type)](#status.415){.xref}
status and include an Accept-Encoding header field in that response,
allowing clients to distinguish between issues related to content
codings and media types. In order to avoid confusion with issues related
to media types, servers that fail a request with a 415 status for
reasons unrelated to content codings [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} include the
Accept-Encoding header field.[¶](#section-12.5.3-15){.pilcrow}

The most common use of Accept-Encoding is in responses with a [415
(Unsupported Media Type)](#status.415){.xref} status code, in response
to optimistic use of a content coding by clients. However, the header
field can also be used to indicate to clients that content codings are
supported in order to optimize future interactions. For example, a
resource might include it in a [2xx (Successful)](#status.2xx){.xref}
response when the request content was big enough to justify use of a
compression coding but the client failed do
so.[¶](#section-12.5.3-16){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.accept-language}
::: {#section-12.5.4 .section}
#### [12.5.4.](#section-12.5.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Accept-Language](#name-accept-language){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-accept-language}

[]{#iref-fields-accept-language-325 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-accept-langua .iref}
[]{#iref-accept-language-header-fiel .iref}

The \"Accept-Language\" header field can be used by user agents to
indicate the set of natural languages that are preferred in the
response. Language tags are defined in [Section
8.5.1](#language.tags){.xref}.[¶](#section-12.5.4-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-accept-language-328 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-language-range-329 .iref}

::: {#section-12.5.4-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Accept-Language = #( language-range [ weight ] )
  language-range  =
            <language-range, see [RFC4647], Section 2.1>
```

[¶](#section-12.5.4-2){.pilcrow}
:::

Each language-range can be given an associated quality value
representing an estimate of the user\'s preference for the languages
specified by that range, as defined in [Section
12.4.2](#quality.values){.xref}. For
example,[¶](#section-12.5.4-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.4-4}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept-Language: da, en-gb;q=0.8, en;q=0.7
```

[¶](#section-12.5.4-4){.pilcrow}
:::

would mean: \"I prefer Danish, but will accept British English and other
types of English\".[¶](#section-12.5.4-5){.pilcrow}

Note that some recipients treat the order in which language tags are
listed as an indication of descending priority, particularly for tags
that are assigned equal quality values (no value is the same as q=1).
However, this behavior cannot be relied upon. For consistency and to
maximize interoperability, many user agents assign each language tag a
unique quality value while also listing them in order of decreasing
quality. Additional discussion of language priority lists can be found
in [Section
2.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4647#section-2.3){.relref} of
\[[RFC4647](#RFC4647){.xref}\].[¶](#section-12.5.4-6){.pilcrow}

For matching, [Section
3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4647#section-3){.relref} of
\[[RFC4647](#RFC4647){.xref}\] defines several matching schemes.
Implementations can offer the most appropriate matching scheme for their
requirements. The \"Basic Filtering\" scheme
(\[[RFC4647](#RFC4647){.xref}\], [Section
3.3.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4647#section-3.3.1){.relref})
is identical to the matching scheme that was previously defined for HTTP
in [Section
14.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2616#section-14.4){.relref} of
\[[RFC2616](#RFC2616){.xref}\].[¶](#section-12.5.4-7){.pilcrow}

It might be contrary to the privacy expectations of the user to send an
Accept-Language header field with the complete linguistic preferences of
the user in every request ([Section
17.13](#fingerprinting){.xref}).[¶](#section-12.5.4-8){.pilcrow}

Since intelligibility is highly dependent on the individual user, user
agents need to allow user control over the linguistic preference (either
through configuration of the user agent itself or by defaulting to a
user controllable system setting). A user agent that does not provide
such control to the user [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} send an Accept-Language
header field.[¶](#section-12.5.4-9){.pilcrow}

**Note:** User agents ought to provide guidance to users when setting a
preference, since users are rarely familiar with the details of language
matching as described above. For example, users might assume that on
selecting \"en-gb\", they will be served any kind of English document if
British English is not available. A user agent might suggest, in such a
case, to add \"en\" to the list for better matching
behavior.[¶](#section-12.5.4-10.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.vary}
::: {#section-12.5.5 .section}
#### [12.5.5.](#section-12.5.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Vary](#name-vary){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-vary}

[]{#iref-fields-vary-330 .iref} []{#iref-header-fields-vary-331 .iref}
[]{#iref-vary-header-field-332 .iref}

The \"Vary\" header field in a response describes what parts of a
request message, aside from the method and target URI, might have
influenced the origin server\'s process for selecting the content of
this response.[¶](#section-12.5.5-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-vary-333 .iref}

::: {#section-12.5.5-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Vary = #( "*" / field-name )
```

[¶](#section-12.5.5-2){.pilcrow}
:::

A Vary field value is either the wildcard member \"\*\" or a list of
request field names, known as the selecting header fields, that might
have had a role in selecting the representation for this response.
Potential selecting header fields are not limited to fields defined by
this specification.[¶](#section-12.5.5-3){.pilcrow}

A list containing the member \"\*\" signals that other aspects of the
request might have played a role in selecting the response
representation, possibly including aspects outside the message syntax
(e.g., the client\'s network address). A recipient will not be able to
determine whether this response is appropriate for a later request
without forwarding the request to the origin server. A proxy [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} generate \"\*\" in a Vary field
value.[¶](#section-12.5.5-4){.pilcrow}

For example, a response that contains[¶](#section-12.5.5-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-12.5.5-6}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Vary: accept-encoding, accept-language
```

[¶](#section-12.5.5-6){.pilcrow}
:::

indicates that the origin server might have used the request\'s
[Accept-Encoding](#field.accept-encoding){.xref} and
[Accept-Language](#field.accept-language){.xref} header fields (or lack
thereof) as determining factors while choosing the content for this
response.[¶](#section-12.5.5-7){.pilcrow}

A Vary field containing a list of field names has two
purposes:[¶](#section-12.5.5-8){.pilcrow}

1.  ::: {#section-12.5.5-9.1}
    To inform cache recipients that they [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} use this
    response to satisfy a later request unless the later request has the
    same values for the listed header fields as the original request
    ([Section
    4.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.1){.relref} of
    \[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]) or reuse of the response has been
    validated by the origin server. In other words, Vary expands the
    cache key required to match a new request to the stored cache
    entry.[¶](#section-12.5.5-9.1.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

2.  ::: {#section-12.5.5-9.2}
    To inform user agent recipients that this response was subject to
    content negotiation ([Section 12](#content.negotiation){.xref}) and
    a different representation might be sent in a subsequent request if
    other values are provided in the listed header fields ([proactive
    negotiation](#proactive.negotiation){.xref}).[¶](#section-12.5.5-9.2.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

An origin server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a Vary header field on a
cacheable response when it wishes that response to be selectively reused
for subsequent requests. Generally, that is the case when the response
content has been tailored to better fit the preferences expressed by
those selecting header fields, such as when an origin server has
selected the response\'s language based on the request\'s
[Accept-Language](#field.accept-language){.xref} header
field.[¶](#section-12.5.5-10){.pilcrow}

Vary might be elided when an origin server considers variance in content
selection to be less significant than Vary\'s performance impact on
caching, particularly when reuse is already limited by cache response
directives ([Section
5.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-5.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-12.5.5-11){.pilcrow}

There is no need to send the Authorization field name in Vary because
reuse of that response for a different user is prohibited by the field
definition ([Section 11.6.2](#field.authorization){.xref}). Likewise, if
the response content has been selected or influenced by network region,
but the origin server wants the cached response to be reused even if
recipients move from one region to another, then there is no need for
the origin server to indicate such variance in
Vary.[¶](#section-12.5.5-12){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#conditional.requests}
::: {#section-13 .section}
## [13.](#section-13){.section-number .selfRef} [Conditional Requests](#name-conditional-requests){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-conditional-requests}

[]{#iref-conditional-request-334 .iref}

A conditional request is an HTTP request with one or more request header
fields that indicate a precondition to be tested before applying the
request method to the target resource. [Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref} defines when to evaluate preconditions and
their order of precedence when more than one precondition is
present.[¶](#section-13-1){.pilcrow}

Conditional GET requests are the most efficient mechanism for HTTP cache
updates \[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]. Conditionals can also be applied
to state-changing methods, such as PUT and DELETE, to prevent the \"lost
update\" problem: one client accidentally overwriting the work of
another client that has been acting in
parallel.[¶](#section-13-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#preconditions}
::: {#section-13.1 .section}
### [13.1.](#section-13.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Preconditions](#name-preconditions){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-preconditions}

[]{#iref-selected-representation-335 .iref}

Preconditions are usually defined with respect to a state of the target
resource as a whole (its current value set) or the state as observed in
a previously obtained representation (one value in that set). If a
resource has multiple current representations, each with its own
observable state, a precondition will assume that the mapping of each
request to a [selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref}
([Section 3.2](#representations){.xref}) is consistent over time.
Regardless, if the mapping is inconsistent or the server is unable to
select an appropriate representation, then no harm will result when the
precondition evaluates to false.[¶](#section-13.1-1){.pilcrow}

Each precondition defined below consists of a comparison between a set
of validators obtained from prior representations of the target resource
to the current state of validators for the selected representation
([Section 8.8](#response.validator){.xref}). Hence, these preconditions
evaluate whether the state of the target resource has changed since a
given state known by the client. The effect of such an evaluation
depends on the method semantics and choice of conditional, as defined in
[Section 13.2](#evaluation){.xref}.[¶](#section-13.1-2){.pilcrow}

Other preconditions, defined by other specifications as extension
fields, might place conditions on all recipients, on the state of the
target resource in general, or on a group of resources. For instance,
the \"If\" header field in WebDAV can make a request conditional on
various aspects of multiple resources, such as locks, if the recipient
understands and implements that field (\[[WEBDAV](#WEBDAV){.xref}\],
[Section
10.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4918#section-10.4){.relref}).[¶](#section-13.1-3){.pilcrow}

Extensibility of preconditions is only possible when the precondition
can be safely ignored if unknown (like
[If-Modified-Since](#field.if-modified-since){.xref}), when deployment
can be assumed for a given use case, or when implementation is signaled
by some other property of the target resource. This encourages a focus
on mutually agreed deployment of common
standards.[¶](#section-13.1-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#field.if-match}
::: {#section-13.1.1 .section}
#### [13.1.1.](#section-13.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [If-Match](#name-if-match){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-if-match}

[]{#iref-fields-if-match-336 .iref} []{#iref-header-fields-if-match-337
.iref} []{#iref-if-match-header-field-338 .iref}

The \"If-Match\" header field makes the request method conditional on
the recipient origin server either having at least one current
representation of the target resource, when the field value is \"\*\",
or having a current representation of the target resource that has an
entity tag matching a member of the list of entity tags provided in the
field value.[¶](#section-13.1.1-1){.pilcrow}

An origin server [MUST]{.bcp14} use the strong comparison function when
comparing entity tags for If-Match ([Section
8.8.3.2](#entity.tag.comparison){.xref}), since the client intends this
precondition to prevent the method from being applied if there have been
any changes to the representation data.[¶](#section-13.1.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-if-match-339 .iref}

::: {#section-13.1.1-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  If-Match = "*" / #entity-tag
```

[¶](#section-13.1.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::

Examples:[¶](#section-13.1.1-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-13.1.1-5}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
If-Match: "xyzzy"
If-Match: "xyzzy", "r2d2xxxx", "c3piozzzz"
If-Match: *
```

[¶](#section-13.1.1-5){.pilcrow}
:::

If-Match is most often used with state-changing methods (e.g., POST,
PUT, DELETE) to prevent accidental overwrites when multiple user agents
might be acting in parallel on the same resource (i.e., to prevent the
\"lost update\" problem). In general, it can be used with any method
that involves the selection or modification of a representation to abort
the request if the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}\'s current entity tag
is not a member within the If-Match field
value.[¶](#section-13.1.1-6){.pilcrow}

When an origin server receives a request that selects a representation
and that request includes an If-Match header field, the origin server
[MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate the If-Match condition per [Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref} prior to performing the
method.[¶](#section-13.1.1-7){.pilcrow}

To evaluate a received If-Match header
field:[¶](#section-13.1.1-8){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the field value is \"\*\", the condition is true if the origin
    server has a current representation for the target
    resource.[¶](#section-13.1.1-9.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.1-9.1}
2.  [If the field value is a list of entity tags, the condition is true
    if any of the listed tags match the entity tag of the selected
    representation.[¶](#section-13.1.1-9.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.1-9.2}
3.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.1-9.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.1-9.3}

An origin server that evaluates an If-Match condition [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
perform the requested method if the condition evaluates to false.
Instead, the origin server [MAY]{.bcp14} indicate that the conditional
request failed by responding with a [412 (Precondition
Failed)](#status.412){.xref} status code. Alternatively, if the request
is a state-changing operation that appears to have already been applied
to the selected representation, the origin server [MAY]{.bcp14} respond
with a [2xx (Successful)](#status.2xx){.xref} status code (i.e., the
change requested by the user agent has already succeeded, but the user
agent might not be aware of it, perhaps because the prior response was
lost or an equivalent change was made by some other user
agent).[¶](#section-13.1.1-10){.pilcrow}

Allowing an origin server to send a success response when a change
request appears to have already been applied is more efficient for many
authoring use cases, but comes with some risk if multiple user agents
are making change requests that are very similar but not cooperative.
For example, multiple user agents writing to a common resource as a
semaphore (e.g., a nonatomic increment) are likely to collide and
potentially lose important state transitions. For those kinds of
resources, an origin server is better off being stringent in sending 412
for every failed precondition on an unsafe method. In other cases,
excluding the ETag field from a success response might encourage the
user agent to perform a GET as its next request to eliminate confusion
about the resource\'s current state.[¶](#section-13.1.1-11){.pilcrow}

A client [MAY]{.bcp14} send an If-Match header field in a
[GET](#GET){.xref} request to indicate that it would prefer a [412
(Precondition Failed)](#status.412){.xref} response if the selected
representation does not match. However, this is only useful in range
requests ([Section 14](#range.requests){.xref}) for completing a
previously received partial representation when there is no desire for a
new representation. [If-Range](#field.if-range){.xref} ([Section
13.1.5](#field.if-range){.xref}) is better suited for range requests
when the client prefers to receive a new
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.1-12){.pilcrow}

A cache or intermediary [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore If-Match because its
interoperability features are only necessary for an origin
server.[¶](#section-13.1.1-13){.pilcrow}

Note that an If-Match header field with a list value containing \"\*\"
and other values (including other instances of \"\*\") is syntactically
invalid (therefore not allowed to be generated) and furthermore is
unlikely to be interoperable.[¶](#section-13.1.1-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.if-none-match}
::: {#section-13.1.2 .section}
#### [13.1.2.](#section-13.1.2){.section-number .selfRef} [If-None-Match](#name-if-none-match){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-if-none-match}

[]{#iref-fields-if-none-match-340 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-if-none-match .iref}
[]{#iref-if-none-match-header-field- .iref}

The \"If-None-Match\" header field makes the request method conditional
on a recipient cache or origin server either not having any current
representation of the target resource, when the field value is \"\*\",
or having a [selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref}
with an entity tag that does not match any of those listed in the field
value.[¶](#section-13.1.2-1){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} use the weak comparison function when
comparing entity tags for If-None-Match ([Section
8.8.3.2](#entity.tag.comparison){.xref}), since weak entity tags can be
used for cache validation even if there have been changes to the
representation data.[¶](#section-13.1.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-if-none-match-343 .iref}

::: {#section-13.1.2-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  If-None-Match = "*" / #entity-tag
```

[¶](#section-13.1.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::

Examples:[¶](#section-13.1.2-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-13.1.2-5}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
If-None-Match: "xyzzy"
If-None-Match: W/"xyzzy"
If-None-Match: "xyzzy", "r2d2xxxx", "c3piozzzz"
If-None-Match: W/"xyzzy", W/"r2d2xxxx", W/"c3piozzzz"
If-None-Match: *
```

[¶](#section-13.1.2-5){.pilcrow}
:::

If-None-Match is primarily used in conditional GET requests to enable
efficient updates of cached information with a minimum amount of
transaction overhead. When a client desires to update one or more stored
responses that have entity tags, the client [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate an
If-None-Match header field containing a list of those entity tags when
making a GET request; this allows recipient servers to send a [304 (Not
Modified)](#status.304){.xref} response to indicate when one of those
stored responses matches the selected
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.2-6){.pilcrow}

If-None-Match can also be used with a value of \"\*\" to prevent an
unsafe request method (e.g., PUT) from inadvertently modifying an
existing representation of the target resource when the client believes
that the resource does not have a current representation ([Section
9.2.1](#safe.methods){.xref}). This is a variation on the \"lost
update\" problem that might arise if more than one client attempts to
create an initial representation for the target
resource.[¶](#section-13.1.2-7){.pilcrow}

When an origin server receives a request that selects a representation
and that request includes an If-None-Match header field, the origin
server [MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate the If-None-Match condition per [Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref} prior to performing the
method.[¶](#section-13.1.2-8){.pilcrow}

To evaluate a received If-None-Match header
field:[¶](#section-13.1.2-9){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the field value is \"\*\", the condition is false if the origin
    server has a current representation for the target
    resource.[¶](#section-13.1.2-10.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.2-10.1}
2.  [If the field value is a list of entity tags, the condition is false
    if one of the listed tags matches the entity tag of the selected
    representation.[¶](#section-13.1.2-10.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.2-10.2}
3.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    true.[¶](#section-13.1.2-10.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.2-10.3}

An origin server that evaluates an If-None-Match condition [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} perform the requested method if the condition evaluates to
false; instead, the origin server [MUST]{.bcp14} respond with either a)
the [304 (Not Modified)](#status.304){.xref} status code if the request
method is GET or HEAD or b) the [412 (Precondition
Failed)](#status.412){.xref} status code for all other request
methods.[¶](#section-13.1.2-11){.pilcrow}

Requirements on cache handling of a received If-None-Match header field
are defined in [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\].[¶](#section-13.1.2-12){.pilcrow}

Note that an If-None-Match header field with a list value containing
\"\*\" and other values (including other instances of \"\*\") is
syntactically invalid (therefore not allowed to be generated) and
furthermore is unlikely to be
interoperable.[¶](#section-13.1.2-13){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.if-modified-since}
::: {#section-13.1.3 .section}
#### [13.1.3.](#section-13.1.3){.section-number .selfRef} [If-Modified-Since](#name-if-modified-since){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-if-modified-since}

[]{#iref-fields-if-modified-since-34 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-if-modified-s .iref}
[]{#iref-if-modified-since-header-fi .iref}

The \"If-Modified-Since\" header field makes a GET or HEAD request
method conditional on the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}\'s modification date
being more recent than the date provided in the field value. Transfer of
the selected representation\'s data is avoided if that data has not
changed.[¶](#section-13.1.3-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-if-modified-since-3 .iref}

::: {#section-13.1.3-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  If-Modified-Since = HTTP-date
```

[¶](#section-13.1.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::

An example of the field is:[¶](#section-13.1.3-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-13.1.3-4}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
If-Modified-Since: Sat, 29 Oct 1994 19:43:31 GMT
```

[¶](#section-13.1.3-4){.pilcrow}
:::

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore If-Modified-Since if the request
contains an [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref} header field;
the condition in [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref} is
considered to be a more accurate replacement for the condition in
If-Modified-Since, and the two are only combined for the sake of
interoperating with older intermediaries that might not implement
[If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref}.[¶](#section-13.1.3-5){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the If-Modified-Since header field if
the received field value is not a valid HTTP-date, the field value has
more than one member, or if the request method is neither GET nor
HEAD.[¶](#section-13.1.3-6){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the If-Modified-Since header field if
the resource does not have a modification date
available.[¶](#section-13.1.3-7){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} interpret an If-Modified-Since field value\'s
timestamp in terms of the origin server\'s
clock.[¶](#section-13.1.3-8){.pilcrow}

If-Modified-Since is typically used for two distinct purposes: 1) to
allow efficient updates of a cached representation that does not have an
entity tag and 2) to limit the scope of a web traversal to resources
that have recently changed.[¶](#section-13.1.3-9){.pilcrow}

When used for cache updates, a cache will typically use the value of the
cached message\'s [Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} header
field to generate the field value of If-Modified-Since. This behavior is
most interoperable for cases where clocks are poorly synchronized or
when the server has chosen to only honor exact timestamp matches (due to
a problem with Last-Modified dates that appear to go \"back in time\"
when the origin server\'s clock is corrected or a representation is
restored from an archived backup). However, caches occasionally generate
the field value based on other data, such as the
[Date](#field.date){.xref} header field of the cached message or the
clock time at which the message was received, particularly when the
cached message does not contain a
[Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} header
field.[¶](#section-13.1.3-10){.pilcrow}

When used for limiting the scope of retrieval to a recent time window, a
user agent will generate an If-Modified-Since field value based on
either its own clock or a [Date](#field.date){.xref} header field
received from the server in a prior response. Origin servers that choose
an exact timestamp match based on the selected representation\'s
[Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} header field will not be
able to help the user agent limit its data transfers to only those
changed during the specified window.[¶](#section-13.1.3-11){.pilcrow}

When an origin server receives a request that selects a representation
and that request includes an If-Modified-Since header field without an
[If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref} header field, the origin
server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} evaluate the If-Modified-Since condition per
[Section 13.2](#evaluation){.xref} prior to performing the
method.[¶](#section-13.1.3-12){.pilcrow}

To evaluate a received If-Modified-Since header
field:[¶](#section-13.1.3-13){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the selected representation\'s last modification date is earlier
    or equal to the date provided in the field value, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.3-14.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.3-14.1}
2.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    true.[¶](#section-13.1.3-14.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.3-14.2}

An origin server that evaluates an If-Modified-Since condition [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} perform the requested method if the condition evaluates to
false; instead, the origin server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a [304 (Not
Modified)](#status.304){.xref} response, including only those metadata
that are useful for identifying or updating a previously cached
response.[¶](#section-13.1.3-15){.pilcrow}

Requirements on cache handling of a received If-Modified-Since header
field are defined in [Section
4.3.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.3.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\].[¶](#section-13.1.3-16){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.if-unmodified-since}
::: {#section-13.1.4 .section}
#### [13.1.4.](#section-13.1.4){.section-number .selfRef} [If-Unmodified-Since](#name-if-unmodified-since){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-if-unmodified-since}

[]{#iref-fields-if-unmodified-since- .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-if-unmodified .iref}
[]{#iref-if-unmodified-since-header- .iref}

The \"If-Unmodified-Since\" header field makes the request method
conditional on the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}\'s last modification
date being earlier than or equal to the date provided in the field
value. This field accomplishes the same purpose as
[If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} for cases where the user agent does
not have an entity tag for the
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.4-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-if-unmodified-since .iref}

::: {#section-13.1.4-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  If-Unmodified-Since = HTTP-date
```

[¶](#section-13.1.4-2){.pilcrow}
:::

An example of the field is:[¶](#section-13.1.4-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-13.1.4-4}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
If-Unmodified-Since: Sat, 29 Oct 1994 19:43:31 GMT
```

[¶](#section-13.1.4-4){.pilcrow}
:::

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore If-Unmodified-Since if the request
contains an [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} header field; the
condition in [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} is considered to be a
more accurate replacement for the condition in If-Unmodified-Since, and
the two are only combined for the sake of interoperating with older
intermediaries that might not implement
[If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref}.[¶](#section-13.1.4-5){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the If-Unmodified-Since header field
if the received field value is not a valid HTTP-date (including when the
field value appears to be a list of
dates).[¶](#section-13.1.4-6){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the If-Unmodified-Since header field
if the resource does not have a modification date
available.[¶](#section-13.1.4-7){.pilcrow}

A recipient [MUST]{.bcp14} interpret an If-Unmodified-Since field
value\'s timestamp in terms of the origin server\'s
clock.[¶](#section-13.1.4-8){.pilcrow}

If-Unmodified-Since is most often used with state-changing methods
(e.g., POST, PUT, DELETE) to prevent accidental overwrites when multiple
user agents might be acting in parallel on a resource that does not
supply entity tags with its representations (i.e., to prevent the \"lost
update\" problem). In general, it can be used with any method that
involves the selection or modification of a representation to abort the
request if the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}\'s last modification
date has changed since the date provided in the If-Unmodified-Since
field value.[¶](#section-13.1.4-9){.pilcrow}

When an origin server receives a request that selects a representation
and that request includes an If-Unmodified-Since header field without an
[If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} header field, the origin server
[MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate the If-Unmodified-Since condition per [Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref} prior to performing the
method.[¶](#section-13.1.4-10){.pilcrow}

To evaluate a received If-Unmodified-Since header
field:[¶](#section-13.1.4-11){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the selected representation\'s last modification date is earlier
    than or equal to the date provided in the field value, the condition
    is true.[¶](#section-13.1.4-12.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.4-12.1}
2.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.4-12.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.4-12.2}

An origin server that evaluates an If-Unmodified-Since condition [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} perform the requested method if the condition evaluates to
false. Instead, the origin server [MAY]{.bcp14} indicate that the
conditional request failed by responding with a [412 (Precondition
Failed)](#status.412){.xref} status code. Alternatively, if the request
is a state-changing operation that appears to have already been applied
to the selected representation, the origin server [MAY]{.bcp14} respond
with a [2xx (Successful)](#status.2xx){.xref} status code (i.e., the
change requested by the user agent has already succeeded, but the user
agent might not be aware of it, perhaps because the prior response was
lost or an equivalent change was made by some other user
agent).[¶](#section-13.1.4-13){.pilcrow}

Allowing an origin server to send a success response when a change
request appears to have already been applied is more efficient for many
authoring use cases, but comes with some risk if multiple user agents
are making change requests that are very similar but not cooperative. In
those cases, an origin server is better off being stringent in sending
412 for every failed precondition on an unsafe
method.[¶](#section-13.1.4-14){.pilcrow}

A client [MAY]{.bcp14} send an If-Unmodified-Since header field in a
[GET](#GET){.xref} request to indicate that it would prefer a [412
(Precondition Failed)](#status.412){.xref} response if the selected
representation has been modified. However, this is only useful in range
requests ([Section 14](#range.requests){.xref}) for completing a
previously received partial representation when there is no desire for a
new representation. [If-Range](#field.if-range){.xref} ([Section
13.1.5](#field.if-range){.xref}) is better suited for range requests
when the client prefers to receive a new
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.4-15){.pilcrow}

A cache or intermediary [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore If-Unmodified-Since because
its interoperability features are only necessary for an origin
server.[¶](#section-13.1.4-16){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.if-range}
::: {#section-13.1.5 .section}
#### [13.1.5.](#section-13.1.5){.section-number .selfRef} [If-Range](#name-if-range){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-if-range}

[]{#iref-fields-if-range-352 .iref} []{#iref-header-fields-if-range-353
.iref} []{#iref-if-range-header-field-354 .iref}

The \"If-Range\" header field provides a special conditional request
mechanism that is similar to the [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} and
[If-Unmodified-Since](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref} header fields
but that instructs the recipient to ignore the
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field if the validator doesn\'t
match, resulting in transfer of the new [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref} instead of a [412
(Precondition Failed)](#status.412){.xref}
response.[¶](#section-13.1.5-1){.pilcrow}

If a client has a partial copy of a representation and wishes to have an
up-to-date copy of the entire representation, it could use the
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field with a conditional GET (using
either or both of
[If-Unmodified-Since](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref} and
[If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref}.) However, if the precondition fails
because the representation has been modified, the client would then have
to make a second request to obtain the entire current
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.5-2){.pilcrow}

The \"If-Range\" header field allows a client to \"short-circuit\" the
second request. Informally, its meaning is as follows: if the
representation is unchanged, send me the part(s) that I am requesting in
Range; otherwise, send me the entire
representation.[¶](#section-13.1.5-3){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-if-range-355 .iref}

::: {#section-13.1.5-4}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  If-Range = entity-tag / HTTP-date
```

[¶](#section-13.1.5-4){.pilcrow}
:::

A valid [entity-tag](#field.etag){.xref} can be distinguished from a
valid [HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref} by examining the first three
characters for a DQUOTE.[¶](#section-13.1.5-5){.pilcrow}

A client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} generate an If-Range header field in a
request that does not contain a [Range](#field.range){.xref} header
field. A server [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore an If-Range header field received
in a request that does not contain a [Range](#field.range){.xref} header
field. An origin server [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore an If-Range header field
received in a request for a target resource that does not support Range
requests.[¶](#section-13.1.5-6){.pilcrow}

A client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} generate an If-Range header field containing
an entity tag that is marked as weak. A client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
generate an If-Range header field containing an
[HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref} unless the client has no entity tag for
the corresponding representation and the date is a strong validator in
the sense defined by [Section
8.8.2.2](#lastmod.comparison){.xref}.[¶](#section-13.1.5-7){.pilcrow}

A server that receives an If-Range header field on a Range request
[MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate the condition per [Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref} prior to performing the
method.[¶](#section-13.1.5-8){.pilcrow}

To evaluate a received If-Range header field containing an
[HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref}:[¶](#section-13.1.5-9){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the [HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref} validator provided is not a
    strong validator in the sense defined by [Section
    8.8.2.2](#lastmod.comparison){.xref}, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.5-10.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.5-10.1}
2.  [If the [HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref} validator provided exactly
    matches the [Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} field value
    for the selected representation, the condition is
    true.[¶](#section-13.1.5-10.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.5-10.2}
3.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.5-10.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.5-10.3}

To evaluate a received If-Range header field containing an
[entity-tag](#field.etag){.xref}:[¶](#section-13.1.5-11){.pilcrow}

1.  [If the [entity-tag](#field.etag){.xref} validator provided exactly
    matches the [ETag](#field.etag){.xref} field value for the selected
    representation using the strong comparison function ([Section
    8.8.3.2](#entity.tag.comparison){.xref}), the condition is
    true.[¶](#section-13.1.5-12.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.5-12.1}
2.  [Otherwise, the condition is
    false.[¶](#section-13.1.5-12.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.1.5-12.2}

A recipient of an If-Range header field [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field if the If-Range condition
evaluates to false. Otherwise, the recipient [SHOULD]{.bcp14} process
the [Range](#field.range){.xref} header field as
requested.[¶](#section-13.1.5-13){.pilcrow}

Note that the If-Range comparison is by exact match, including when the
validator is an [HTTP-date](#http.date){.xref}, and so it differs from
the \"earlier than or equal to\" comparison used when evaluating an
[If-Unmodified-Since](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref}
conditional.[¶](#section-13.1.5-14){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#evaluation}
::: {#section-13.2 .section}
### [13.2.](#section-13.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Evaluation of Preconditions](#name-evaluation-of-preconditions){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-evaluation-of-preconditions}

::: {#when.to.evaluate}
::: {#section-13.2.1 .section}
#### [13.2.1.](#section-13.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [When to Evaluate](#name-when-to-evaluate){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-when-to-evaluate}

Except when excluded below, a recipient cache or origin server
[MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate received request preconditions after it has
successfully performed its normal request checks and just before it
would process the request content (if any) or perform the action
associated with the request method. A server [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore all
received preconditions if its response to the same request without those
conditions, prior to processing the request content, would have been a
status code other than a [2xx (Successful)](#status.2xx){.xref} or [412
(Precondition Failed)](#status.412){.xref}. In other words, redirects
and failures that can be detected before significant processing occurs
take precedence over the evaluation of
preconditions.[¶](#section-13.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

A server that is not the origin server for the target resource and
cannot act as a cache for requests on the target resource [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} evaluate the conditional request header fields defined by
this specification, and it [MUST]{.bcp14} forward them if the request is
forwarded, since the generating client intends that they be evaluated by
a server that can provide a current representation. Likewise, a server
[MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the conditional request header fields defined by
this specification when received with a request method that does not
involve the selection or modification of a [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}, such as CONNECT,
OPTIONS, or TRACE.[¶](#section-13.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

Note that protocol extensions can modify the conditions under which
preconditions are evaluated or the consequences of their evaluation. For
example, the immutable cache directive (defined by
\[[RFC8246](#RFC8246){.xref}\]) instructs caches to forgo forwarding
conditional requests when they hold a fresh
response.[¶](#section-13.2.1-3){.pilcrow}

Although conditional request header fields are defined as being usable
with the HEAD method (to keep HEAD\'s semantics consistent with those of
GET), there is no point in sending a conditional HEAD because a
successful response is around the same size as a [304 (Not
Modified)](#status.304){.xref} response and more useful than a [412
(Precondition Failed)](#status.412){.xref}
response.[¶](#section-13.2.1-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#precedence}
::: {#section-13.2.2 .section}
#### [13.2.2.](#section-13.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Precedence of Preconditions](#name-precedence-of-preconditions){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-precedence-of-preconditions}

When more than one conditional request header field is present in a
request, the order in which the fields are evaluated becomes important.
In practice, the fields defined in this document are consistently
implemented in a single, logical order, since \"lost update\"
preconditions have more strict requirements than cache validation, a
validated cache is more efficient than a partial response, and entity
tags are presumed to be more accurate than date
validators.[¶](#section-13.2.2-1){.pilcrow}

A recipient cache or origin server [MUST]{.bcp14} evaluate the request
preconditions defined by this specification in the following
order:[¶](#section-13.2.2-2){.pilcrow}

1.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.1}
    ::: {#precedence1}
    When recipient is the origin server and
    [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} is present, evaluate the
    [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref}
    precondition:[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.1.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [if true, continue to step
        [3](#precedence3){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.1.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.1.2.1}
    -   [if false, respond [412 (Precondition
        Failed)](#status.412){.xref} unless it can be determined that
        the state-changing request has already succeeded (see [Section
        13.1.1](#field.if-match){.xref})[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.1.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.1.2.2}
    :::
    :::

2.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.2}
    ::: {#precedence2}
    When recipient is the origin server,
    [If-Match](#field.if-match){.xref} is not present, and
    [If-Unmodified-Since](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref} is present,
    evaluate the
    [If-Unmodified-Since](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref}
    precondition:[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.2.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [if true, continue to step
        [3](#precedence3){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.2.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.2.2.1}
    -   [if false, respond [412 (Precondition
        Failed)](#status.412){.xref} unless it can be determined that
        the state-changing request has already succeeded (see [Section
        13.1.4](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref})[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.2.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.2.2.2}
    :::
    :::

3.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.3}
    ::: {#precedence3}
    When [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref} is present,
    evaluate the [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref}
    precondition:[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.3.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [if true, continue to step
        [5](#precedence5){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.1}
    -   [if false for GET/HEAD, respond [304 (Not
        Modified)](#status.304){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.2}
    -   [if false for other methods, respond [412 (Precondition
        Failed)](#status.412){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.3.2.3}
    :::
    :::

4.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.4}
    ::: {#precedence4}
    When the method is GET or HEAD,
    [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref} is not present, and
    [If-Modified-Since](#field.if-modified-since){.xref} is present,
    evaluate the [If-Modified-Since](#field.if-modified-since){.xref}
    precondition:[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.4.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [if true, continue to step
        [5](#precedence5){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.4.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.4.2.1}
    -   [if false, respond [304 (Not
        Modified)](#status.304){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.4.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.4.2.2}
    :::
    :::

5.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.5}
    ::: {#precedence5}
    When the method is GET and both [Range](#field.range){.xref} and
    [If-Range](#field.if-range){.xref} are present, evaluate the
    [If-Range](#field.if-range){.xref}
    precondition:[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.5.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [if true and the [Range](#field.range){.xref} is applicable to
        the [selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref},
        respond [206 (Partial
        Content)](#status.206){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.5.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.5.2.1}
    -   [otherwise, ignore the [Range](#field.range){.xref} header field
        and respond [200
        (OK)](#status.200){.xref}[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.5.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.5.2.2}
    :::
    :::

6.  ::: {#section-13.2.2-3.6}
    ::: {#precedencelast}
    Otherwise,[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.6.1){.pilcrow}

    -   [perform the requested method and respond according to its
        success or
        failure.[¶](#section-13.2.2-3.6.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-13.2.2-3.6.2.1}
    :::
    :::

Any extension to HTTP that defines additional conditional request header
fields ought to define the order for evaluating such fields in relation
to those defined in this document and other conditionals that might be
found in practice.[¶](#section-13.2.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#range.requests}
::: {#section-14 .section}
## [14.](#section-14){.section-number .selfRef} [Range Requests](#name-range-requests){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-range-requests}

Clients often encounter interrupted data transfers as a result of
canceled requests or dropped connections. When a client has stored a
partial representation, it is desirable to request the remainder of that
representation in a subsequent request rather than transfer the entire
representation. Likewise, devices with limited local storage might
benefit from being able to request only a subset of a larger
representation, such as a single page of a very large document, or the
dimensions of an embedded image.[¶](#section-14-1){.pilcrow}

Range requests are an [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} feature of HTTP, designed so
that recipients not implementing this feature (or not supporting it for
the target resource) can respond as if it is a normal GET request
without impacting interoperability. Partial responses are indicated by a
distinct status code to not be mistaken for full responses by caches
that might not implement the feature.[¶](#section-14-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#range.units}
::: {#section-14.1 .section}
### [14.1.](#section-14.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Range Units](#name-range-units){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-range-units}

Representation data can be partitioned into subranges when there are
addressable structural units inherent to that data\'s content coding or
media type. For example, octet (a.k.a. byte) boundaries are a structural
unit common to all representation data, allowing partitions of the data
to be identified as a range of bytes at some offset from the start or
end of that data.[¶](#section-14.1-1){.pilcrow}

This general notion of a \"range unit\" is used in the
[Accept-Ranges](#field.accept-ranges){.xref} ([Section
14.3](#field.accept-ranges){.xref}) response header field to advertise
support for range requests, the [Range](#field.range){.xref} ([Section
14.2](#field.range){.xref}) request header field to delineate the parts
of a representation that are requested, and the
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} ([Section
14.4](#field.content-range){.xref}) header field to describe which part
of a representation is being transferred.[¶](#section-14.1-2){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-range-unit-356 .iref}

::: {#section-14.1-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  range-unit       = token
```

[¶](#section-14.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::

All range unit names are case-insensitive and ought to be registered
within the \"HTTP Range Unit Registry\", as defined in [Section
16.5.1](#range.unit.registry){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1-4){.pilcrow}

Range units are intended to be extensible, as described in [Section
16.5](#range.unit.extensibility){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#range.specifiers}
::: {#section-14.1.1 .section}
#### [14.1.1.](#section-14.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Range Specifiers](#name-range-specifiers){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-range-specifiers}

[]{#iref-satisfiable-range-357 .iref} []{#iref-unsatisfiable-range-358
.iref}

Ranges are expressed in terms of a range unit paired with a set of range
specifiers. The range unit name determines what kinds of range-spec are
applicable to its own specifiers. Hence, the following grammar is
generic: each range unit is expected to specify requirements on when
[int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref},
[suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}, and
[other-range](#rule.other-range){.xref} are
allowed.[¶](#section-14.1.1-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#rule.ranges-specifier}
A range request can specify a single range or a set of ranges within a
single representation.[¶](#section-14.1.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::

[]{#iref-grammar-ranges-specifier-35 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-range-set-360 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-range-spec-361
.iref}

::: {#section-14.1.1-3}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  ranges-specifier = range-unit "=" range-set
  range-set        = 1#range-spec
  range-spec       = int-range
                   / suffix-range
                   / other-range
```

[¶](#section-14.1.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#rule.int-range}
An [int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref} is a range expressed as two
non-negative integers or as one non-negative integer through to the end
of the representation data. The range unit specifies what the integers
mean (e.g., they might indicate unit offsets from the beginning,
inclusive numbered parts, etc.).[¶](#section-14.1.1-4){.pilcrow}
:::

[]{#iref-grammar-int-range-362 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-first-pos-363
.iref} []{#iref-grammar-last-pos-364 .iref}

::: {#section-14.1.1-5}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  int-range     = first-pos "-" [ last-pos ]
  first-pos     = 1*DIGIT
  last-pos      = 1*DIGIT
```

[¶](#section-14.1.1-5){.pilcrow}
:::

An [int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref} is invalid if the
[last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value is present and less than the
[first-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1.1-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#rule.suffix-range}
A [suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref} is a range expressed as a
suffix of the representation data with the provided non-negative integer
maximum length (in range units). In other words, the last N units of the
representation data.[¶](#section-14.1.1-7){.pilcrow}
:::

[]{#iref-grammar-suffix-range-365 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-suffix-length-366 .iref}

::: {#section-14.1.1-8}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  suffix-range  = "-" suffix-length
  suffix-length = 1*DIGIT
```

[¶](#section-14.1.1-8){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#rule.other-range}
To provide for extensibility, the
[other-range](#rule.other-range){.xref} rule is a mostly unconstrained
grammar that allows application-specific or future range units to define
additional range specifiers.[¶](#section-14.1.1-9){.pilcrow}
:::

[]{#iref-grammar-other-range-367 .iref}

::: {#section-14.1.1-10}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  other-range   = 1*( %x21-2B / %x2D-7E )
                ; 1*(VCHAR excluding comma)
```

[¶](#section-14.1.1-10){.pilcrow}
:::

A [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} is invalid if it
contains any [range-spec](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} that is invalid
or undefined for the indicated
[range-unit](#range.units){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1.1-11){.pilcrow}

::: {#satisfiable}
A valid [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} is
\"satisfiable\" if it contains at least one
[range-spec](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} that is satisfiable, as
defined by the indicated [range-unit](#range.units){.xref}. Otherwise,
the [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} is
\"unsatisfiable\".[¶](#section-14.1.1-12){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#byte.ranges}
::: {#section-14.1.2 .section}
#### [14.1.2.](#section-14.1.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Byte Ranges](#name-byte-ranges){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-byte-ranges}

The \"bytes\" range unit is used to express subranges of a
representation data\'s octet sequence. Each byte range is expressed as
an integer range at some offset, relative to either the beginning
([int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref}) or end
([suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}) of the representation data.
Byte ranges do not use the [other-range](#rule.other-range){.xref}
specifier.[¶](#section-14.1.2-1){.pilcrow}

The [first-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value in a bytes
[int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref} gives the offset of the first byte
in a range. The [last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value gives the
offset of the last byte in the range; that is, the byte positions
specified are inclusive. Byte offsets start at
zero.[¶](#section-14.1.2-2){.pilcrow}

If the representation data has a content coding applied, each byte range
is calculated with respect to the encoded sequence of bytes, not the
sequence of underlying bytes that would be obtained after
decoding.[¶](#section-14.1.2-3){.pilcrow}

Examples of bytes range specifiers:[¶](#section-14.1.2-4){.pilcrow}

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-5.1}
    The first 500 bytes (byte offsets 0-499,
    inclusive):[¶](#section-14.1.2-5.1.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-5.1.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=0-499

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-5.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-5.2}
    The second 500 bytes (byte offsets 500-999,
    inclusive):[¶](#section-14.1.2-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-5.2.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=500-999

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-5.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

A client can limit the number of bytes requested without knowing the
size of the [selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref}.
If the [last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value is absent, or if the
value is greater than or equal to the current length of the
representation data, the byte range is interpreted as the remainder of
the representation (i.e., the server replaces the value of
[last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} with a value that is one less than
the current length of the selected
representation).[¶](#section-14.1.2-6){.pilcrow}

A client can refer to the last N bytes (N \> 0) of the selected
representation using a [suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}. If the
selected representation is shorter than the specified
[suffix-length](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}, the entire representation is
used.[¶](#section-14.1.2-7){.pilcrow}

Additional examples, assuming a representation of length
10000:[¶](#section-14.1.2-8){.pilcrow}

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.1}
    The final 500 bytes (byte offsets 9500-9999,
    inclusive):[¶](#section-14.1.2-9.1.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.1.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=-500

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-9.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Or:[¶](#section-14.1.2-9.1.3){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.1.4 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=9500-

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-9.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.2}
    The first and last bytes only (bytes 0 and
    9999):[¶](#section-14.1.2-9.2.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.2.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=0-0,-1

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-9.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.3}
    The first, middle, and last 1000
    bytes:[¶](#section-14.1.2-9.3.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.3.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes= 0-999, 4500-5499, -1000

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-9.3.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.4}
    Other valid (but not canonical) specifications of the second 500
    bytes (byte offsets 500-999,
    inclusive):[¶](#section-14.1.2-9.4.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.1.2-9.4.2 .alignLeft .art-text .artwork}
             bytes=500-600,601-999
             bytes=500-700,601-999

    [¶](#section-14.1.2-9.4.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

For a [GET](#GET){.xref} request, a valid bytes
[range-spec](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} is
[satisfiable](#satisfiable){.xref} if it is
either:[¶](#section-14.1.2-10){.pilcrow}

-   [an [int-range](#rule.int-range){.xref} with a
    [first-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} that is less than the current
    length of the selected representation
    or[¶](#section-14.1.2-11.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-14.1.2-11.1}
-   [a [suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref} with a non-zero
    [suffix-length](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1.2-11.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-14.1.2-11.2}

When a selected representation has zero length, the only
[satisfiable](#satisfiable){.xref} form of
[range-spec](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} in a [GET](#GET){.xref}
request is a [suffix-range](#rule.suffix-range){.xref} with a non-zero
[suffix-length](#rule.suffix-range){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.1.2-12){.pilcrow}

In the byte-range syntax, [first-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref},
[last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref}, and
[suffix-length](#rule.suffix-range){.xref} are expressed as decimal
number of octets. Since there is no predefined limit to the length of
content, recipients [MUST]{.bcp14} anticipate potentially large decimal
numerals and prevent parsing errors due to integer conversion
overflows.[¶](#section-14.1.2-13){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#field.range}
::: {#section-14.2 .section}
### [14.2.](#section-14.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Range](#name-range){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-range}

[]{#iref-fields-range-368 .iref} []{#iref-header-fields-range-369 .iref}
[]{#iref-range-header-field-370 .iref}

The \"Range\" header field on a GET request modifies the method
semantics to request transfer of only one or more subranges of the
selected representation data ([Section
8.1](#representation.data){.xref}), rather than the entire [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-range-371 .iref}

::: {#section-14.2-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Range = ranges-specifier
```

[¶](#section-14.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::

A server [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore the Range header field. However, origin
servers and intermediate caches ought to support byte ranges when
possible, since they support efficient recovery from partially failed
transfers and partial retrieval of large
representations.[¶](#section-14.2-3){.pilcrow}

A server [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore a Range header field received with a
request method that is unrecognized or for which range handling is not
defined. For this specification, [GET](#GET){.xref} is the only method
for which range handling is defined.[¶](#section-14.2-4){.pilcrow}

An origin server [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore a Range header field that
contains a range unit it does not understand. A proxy [MAY]{.bcp14}
discard a Range header field that contains a range unit it does not
understand.[¶](#section-14.2-5){.pilcrow}

A server that supports range requests [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore or reject a
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field that contains an invalid
[ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} ([Section
14.1.1](#range.specifiers){.xref}), a
[ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} with more than two
overlapping ranges, or a set of many small ranges that are not listed in
ascending order, since these are indications of either a broken client
or a deliberate denial-of-service attack ([Section
17.15](#overlapping.ranges){.xref}). A client [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14}
request multiple ranges that are inherently less efficient to process
and transfer than a single range that encompasses the same
data.[¶](#section-14.2-6){.pilcrow}

A server that supports range requests [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore a
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field when the selected
representation has no content (i.e., the selected representation\'s data
is of zero length).[¶](#section-14.2-7){.pilcrow}

A client that is requesting multiple ranges [SHOULD]{.bcp14} list those
ranges in ascending order (the order in which they would typically be
received in a complete representation) unless there is a specific need
to request a later part earlier. For example, a user agent processing a
large representation with an internal catalog of parts might need to
request later parts first, particularly if the representation consists
of pages stored in reverse order and the user agent wishes to transfer
