one page at a time.[¶](#section-14.2-8){.pilcrow}

The Range header field is evaluated after evaluating the precondition
header fields defined in [Section 13.1](#preconditions){.xref}, and only
if the result in absence of the Range header field would be a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response. In other words, Range is ignored
when a conditional GET would result in a [304 (Not
Modified)](#status.304){.xref} response.[¶](#section-14.2-9){.pilcrow}

The If-Range header field ([Section 13.1.5](#field.if-range){.xref}) can
be used as a precondition to applying the Range header
field.[¶](#section-14.2-10){.pilcrow}

If all of the preconditions are true, the server supports the Range
header field for the target resource, the received Range field-value
contains a valid [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} with
a [range-unit](#range.units){.xref} supported for that target resource,
and that [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref} is
[satisfiable](#satisfiable){.xref} with respect to the selected
representation, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a [206 (Partial
Content)](#status.206){.xref} response with content containing one or
more partial representations that correspond to the satisfiable
[range-spec](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref}(s)
requested.[¶](#section-14.2-11){.pilcrow}

The above does not imply that a server will send all requested ranges.
In some cases, it may only be possible (or efficient) to send a portion
of the requested ranges first, while expecting the client to re-request
the remaining portions later if they are still desired (see [Section
15.3.7](#status.206){.xref}).[¶](#section-14.2-12){.pilcrow}

If all of the preconditions are true, the server supports the Range
header field for the target resource, the received Range field-value
contains a valid [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref}, and
either the [range-unit](#range.units){.xref} is not supported for that
target resource or the [ranges-specifier](#rule.ranges-specifier){.xref}
is unsatisfiable with respect to the selected representation, the server
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a [416 (Range Not
Satisfiable)](#status.416){.xref}
response.[¶](#section-14.2-13){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.accept-ranges}
::: {#section-14.3 .section}
### [14.3.](#section-14.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Accept-Ranges](#name-accept-ranges){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-accept-ranges}

[]{#iref-fields-accept-ranges-372 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-accept-ranges .iref}
[]{#iref-accept-ranges-header-field- .iref}

The \"Accept-Ranges\" field in a response indicates whether an upstream
server supports range requests for the target
resource.[¶](#section-14.3-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-accept-ranges-375 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-acceptable-ranges-3 .iref}

::: {#section-14.3-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Accept-Ranges     = acceptable-ranges
  acceptable-ranges = 1#range-unit
```

[¶](#section-14.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::

For example, a server that supports [byte-range
requests](#byte.ranges){.xref} ([Section 14.1.2](#byte.ranges){.xref})
can send the field[¶](#section-14.3-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.3-4}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept-Ranges: bytes
```

[¶](#section-14.3-4){.pilcrow}
:::

to indicate that it supports byte range requests for that target
resource, thereby encouraging its use by the client for future partial
requests on the same request path. Range units are defined in [Section
14.1](#range.units){.xref}.[¶](#section-14.3-5){.pilcrow}

A client [MAY]{.bcp14} generate range requests regardless of having
received an Accept-Ranges field. The information only provides advice
for the sake of improving performance and reducing unnecessary network
transfers.[¶](#section-14.3-6){.pilcrow}

Conversely, a client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} assume that receiving an
Accept-Ranges field means that future range requests will return partial
responses. The content might change, the server might only support range
requests at certain times or under certain conditions, or a different
intermediary might process the next
request.[¶](#section-14.3-7){.pilcrow}

A server that does not support any kind of range request for the target
resource [MAY]{.bcp14} send[¶](#section-14.3-8){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.3-9}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Accept-Ranges: none
```

[¶](#section-14.3-9){.pilcrow}
:::

to advise the client not to attempt a range request on the same request
path. The range unit \"none\" is reserved for this
purpose.[¶](#section-14.3-10){.pilcrow}

The Accept-Ranges field [MAY]{.bcp14} be sent in a trailer section, but
is preferred to be sent as a header field because the information is
particularly useful for restarting large information transfers that have
failed in mid-content (before the trailer section is
received).[¶](#section-14.3-11){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#field.content-range}
::: {#section-14.4 .section}
### [14.4.](#section-14.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Content-Range](#name-content-range){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-content-range}

[]{#iref-fields-content-range-377 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-content-range .iref}
[]{#iref-content-range-header-field- .iref}

The \"Content-Range\" header field is sent in a single part [206
(Partial Content)](#status.206){.xref} response to indicate the partial
range of the [selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref}
enclosed as the message content, sent in each part of a multipart 206
response to indicate the range enclosed within each body part ([Section
14.6](#multipart.byteranges){.xref}), and sent in [416 (Range Not
Satisfiable)](#status.416){.xref} responses to provide information about
the selected representation.[¶](#section-14.4-1){.pilcrow}

[]{#iref-grammar-content-range-380 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-range-resp-381 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-incl-range-382
.iref} []{#iref-grammar-unsatisfied-range-3 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-complete-length-384 .iref}
[]{#iref-grammar-first-pos-385 .iref} []{#iref-grammar-last-pos-386
.iref}

::: {#section-14.4-2}
``` {.lang-abnf9110 .sourcecode}
  Content-Range       = range-unit SP
                        ( range-resp / unsatisfied-range )

  range-resp          = incl-range "/" ( complete-length / "*" )
  incl-range          = first-pos "-" last-pos
  unsatisfied-range   = "*/" complete-length

  complete-length     = 1*DIGIT
```

[¶](#section-14.4-2){.pilcrow}
:::

If a [206 (Partial Content)](#status.206){.xref} response contains a
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field with a [range
unit](#range.units){.xref} ([Section 14.1](#range.units){.xref}) that
the recipient does not understand, the recipient [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
attempt to recombine it with a stored representation. A proxy that
receives such a message [SHOULD]{.bcp14} forward it
downstream.[¶](#section-14.4-3){.pilcrow}

Content-Range might also be sent as a request modifier to request a
partial PUT, as described in [Section 14.5](#partial.PUT){.xref}, based
on private agreements between client and origin server. A server
[MUST]{.bcp14} ignore a Content-Range header field received in a request
with a method for which Content-Range support is not
defined.[¶](#section-14.4-4){.pilcrow}

For byte ranges, a sender [SHOULD]{.bcp14} indicate the complete length
of the representation from which the range has been extracted, unless
the complete length is unknown or difficult to determine. An asterisk
character (\"\*\") in place of the complete-length indicates that the
representation length was unknown when the header field was
generated.[¶](#section-14.4-5){.pilcrow}

The following example illustrates when the complete length of the
selected representation is known by the sender to be 1234
bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.4-7}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Content-Range: bytes 42-1233/1234
```

[¶](#section-14.4-7){.pilcrow}
:::

and this second example illustrates when the complete length is
unknown:[¶](#section-14.4-8){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.4-9}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Content-Range: bytes 42-1233/*
```

[¶](#section-14.4-9){.pilcrow}
:::

A Content-Range field value is invalid if it contains a
[range-resp](#field.content-range){.xref} that has a
[last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value less than its
[first-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value, or a
[complete-length](#field.content-range){.xref} value less than or equal
to its [last-pos](#rule.int-range){.xref} value. The recipient of an
invalid [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
attempt to recombine the received content with a stored
representation.[¶](#section-14.4-10){.pilcrow}

A server generating a [416 (Range Not Satisfiable)](#status.416){.xref}
response to a byte-range request [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a Content-Range
header field with an [unsatisfied-range](#field.content-range){.xref}
value, as in the following example:[¶](#section-14.4-11){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.4-12}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
Content-Range: bytes */1234
```

[¶](#section-14.4-12){.pilcrow}
:::

The complete-length in a 416 response indicates the current length of
the selected representation.[¶](#section-14.4-13){.pilcrow}

The Content-Range header field has no meaning for status codes that do
not explicitly describe its semantic. For this specification, only the
[206 (Partial Content)](#status.206){.xref} and [416 (Range Not
Satisfiable)](#status.416){.xref} status codes describe a meaning for
Content-Range.[¶](#section-14.4-14){.pilcrow}

The following are examples of Content-Range values in which the selected
representation contains a total of 1234
bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-15){.pilcrow}

-   ::: {#section-14.4-16.1}
    The first 500 bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-16.1.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.4-16.1.2}
    ``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
    Content-Range: bytes 0-499/1234
    ```

    [¶](#section-14.4-16.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.4-16.2}
    The second 500 bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-16.2.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.4-16.2.2}
    ``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
    Content-Range: bytes 500-999/1234
    ```

    [¶](#section-14.4-16.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.4-16.3}
    All except for the first 500
    bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-16.3.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.4-16.3.2}
    ``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
    Content-Range: bytes 500-1233/1234
    ```

    [¶](#section-14.4-16.3.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

-   ::: {#section-14.4-16.4}
    The last 500 bytes:[¶](#section-14.4-16.4.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-14.4-16.4.2}
    ``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
    Content-Range: bytes 734-1233/1234
    ```

    [¶](#section-14.4-16.4.2){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::
:::
:::

::: {#partial.PUT}
::: {#section-14.5 .section}
### [14.5.](#section-14.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Partial PUT](#name-partial-put){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-partial-put}

[]{#iref-fields-content-range-387 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-content-range- .iref}
[]{#iref-content-range-header-field-3 .iref}

Some origin servers support [PUT](#PUT){.xref} of a partial
representation when the user agent sends a
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field ([Section
14.4](#field.content-range){.xref}) in the request, though such support
is inconsistent and depends on private agreements with user agents. In
general, it requests that the state of the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} be partly replaced with the enclosed
content at an offset and length indicated by the Content-Range value,
where the offset is relative to the current selected
representation.[¶](#section-14.5-1){.pilcrow}

An origin server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} respond with a [400 (Bad
Request)](#status.400){.xref} status code if it receives
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} on a PUT for a target
resource that does not support partial PUT
requests.[¶](#section-14.5-2){.pilcrow}

Partial PUT is not backwards compatible with the original definition of
PUT. It may result in the content being written as a complete
replacement for the current
representation.[¶](#section-14.5-3){.pilcrow}

Partial resource updates are also possible by targeting a separately
identified resource with state that overlaps or extends a portion of the
larger resource, or by using a different method that has been
specifically defined for partial updates (for example, the PATCH method
defined in
\[[RFC5789](#RFC5789){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-14.5-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#multipart.byteranges}
::: {#section-14.6 .section}
### [14.6.](#section-14.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Media Type multipart/byteranges](#name-media-type-multipart-bytera){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-media-type-multipart-bytera}

[]{#iref-media-type-multipart-bytera .iref}
[]{#iref-multipart-byteranges-media- .iref}

When a [206 (Partial Content)](#status.206){.xref} response message
includes the content of multiple ranges, they are transmitted as body
parts in a multipart message body (\[[RFC2046](#RFC2046){.xref}\],
[Section
5.1](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2046#section-5.1){.relref}) with
the media type of
\"multipart/byteranges\".[¶](#section-14.6-1){.pilcrow}

The \"multipart/byteranges\" media type includes one or more body parts,
each with its own [Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref} and
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} fields. The required
boundary parameter specifies the boundary string used to separate each
body part.[¶](#section-14.6-2){.pilcrow}

Implementation Notes:[¶](#section-14.6-3){.pilcrow}

1.  [Additional CRLFs might precede the first boundary string in the
    body.[¶](#section-14.6-4.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-14.6-4.1}
2.  [Although \[[RFC2046](#RFC2046){.xref}\] permits the boundary string
    to be quoted, some existing implementations handle a quoted boundary
    string
    incorrectly.[¶](#section-14.6-4.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-14.6-4.2}
3.  [A number of clients and servers were coded to an early draft of the
    byteranges specification that used a media type of
    \"multipart/x-byteranges\"[]{#iref-multipart-x-byteranges-medi
    .iref}[]{#iref-media-type-multipart-x-byte .iref}, which is almost
    (but not quite) compatible with this
    type.[¶](#section-14.6-4.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-14.6-4.3}

Despite the name, the \"multipart/byteranges\" media type is not limited
to byte ranges. The following example uses an \"exampleunit\" range
unit:[¶](#section-14.6-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-14.6-6}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
HTTP/1.1 206 Partial Content
Date: Tue, 14 Nov 1995 06:25:24 GMT
Last-Modified: Tue, 14 July 04:58:08 GMT
Content-Length: 2331785
Content-Type: multipart/byteranges; boundary=THIS_STRING_SEPARATES

--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES
Content-Type: video/example
Content-Range: exampleunit 1.2-4.3/25

...the first range...
--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES
Content-Type: video/example
Content-Range: exampleunit 11.2-14.3/25

...the second range
--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES--
```

[¶](#section-14.6-6){.pilcrow}
:::

The following information serves as the registration form for the
\"multipart/byteranges\" media type.[¶](#section-14.6-7){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

Type name:
:   multipart[¶](#section-14.6-8.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Subtype name:
:   byteranges[¶](#section-14.6-8.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Required parameters:
:   boundary[¶](#section-14.6-8.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Optional parameters:
:   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.8){.pilcrow}
:   

Encoding considerations:
:   only \"7bit\", \"8bit\", or \"binary\" are
    permitted[¶](#section-14.6-8.10){.pilcrow}
:   

Security considerations:
:   see [Section
    17](#security.considerations){.xref}[¶](#section-14.6-8.12){.pilcrow}
:   

Interoperability considerations:
:   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.14){.pilcrow}
:   

Published specification:
:   RFC 9110 (see [Section
    14.6](#multipart.byteranges){.xref})[¶](#section-14.6-8.16){.pilcrow}
:   

Applications that use this media type:
:   HTTP components supporting multiple ranges in a single
    request[¶](#section-14.6-8.18){.pilcrow}
:   

Fragment identifier considerations:
:   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.20){.pilcrow}
:   

Additional information:
:   []{.break}

    Deprecated alias names for this type:
    :   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.22.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    Magic number(s):
    :   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.22.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    File extension(s):
    :   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.22.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   

    Macintosh file type code(s):
    :   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.22.1.8){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Person and email address to contact for further information:
:   See Authors\' Addresses section.[¶](#section-14.6-8.24){.pilcrow}
:   

Intended usage:
:   COMMON[¶](#section-14.6-8.26){.pilcrow}
:   

Restrictions on usage:
:   N/A[¶](#section-14.6-8.28){.pilcrow}
:   

Author:
:   See Authors\' Addresses section.[¶](#section-14.6-8.30){.pilcrow}
:   

Change controller:
:   IESG[¶](#section-14.6-8.32){.pilcrow}
:   
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#status.codes}
::: {#section-15 .section}
## [15.](#section-15){.section-number .selfRef} [Status Codes](#name-status-codes){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-status-codes}

[]{#iref-status-code-394 .iref}

The status code of a response is a three-digit integer code that
describes the result of the request and the semantics of the response,
including whether the request was successful and what content is
enclosed (if any). All valid status codes are within the range of 100 to
599, inclusive.[¶](#section-15-1){.pilcrow}

The first digit of the status code defines the class of response. The
last two digits do not have any categorization role. There are five
values for the first digit:[¶](#section-15-2){.pilcrow}

-   [[1xx (Informational)](#status.1xx){.xref}: The request was
    received, continuing
    process[¶](#section-15-3.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-15-3.1}
-   [[2xx (Successful)](#status.2xx){.xref}: The request was
    successfully received, understood, and
    accepted[¶](#section-15-3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-15-3.2}
-   [[3xx (Redirection)](#status.3xx){.xref}: Further action needs to be
    taken in order to complete the
    request[¶](#section-15-3.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-15-3.3}
-   [[4xx (Client Error)](#status.4xx){.xref}: The request contains bad
    syntax or cannot be
    fulfilled[¶](#section-15-3.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-15-3.4}
-   [[5xx (Server Error)](#status.5xx){.xref}: The server failed to
    fulfill an apparently valid
    request[¶](#section-15-3.5){.pilcrow}]{#section-15-3.5}

HTTP status codes are extensible. A client is not required to understand
the meaning of all registered status codes, though such understanding is
obviously desirable. However, a client [MUST]{.bcp14} understand the
class of any status code, as indicated by the first digit, and treat an
unrecognized status code as being equivalent to the x00 status code of
that class.[¶](#section-15-4){.pilcrow}

For example, if a client receives an unrecognized status code of 471, it
can see from the first digit that there was something wrong with its
request and treat the response as if it had received a [400 (Bad
Request)](#status.400){.xref} status code. The response message will
usually contain a representation that explains the
status.[¶](#section-15-5){.pilcrow}

Values outside the range 100..599 are invalid. Implementations often use
three-digit integer values outside of that range (i.e., 600..999) for
internal communication of non-HTTP status (e.g., library errors). A
client that receives a response with an invalid status code
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} process the response as if it had a [5xx (Server
Error)](#status.5xx){.xref} status code.[¶](#section-15-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#final.interim}
[]{#iref-status-codes-final-395 .iref} []{#iref-status-codes-interim-396
.iref} []{#iref-status-codes-informational- .iref} A single request can
have multiple associated responses: zero or more \"interim\" (non-final)
responses with status codes in the \"informational\"
([1xx](#status.1xx){.xref}) range, followed by exactly one \"final\"
response with a status code in one of the other
ranges.[¶](#section-15-7){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#overview.of.status.codes}
::: {#section-15.1 .section}
### [15.1.](#section-15.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Overview of Status Codes](#name-overview-of-status-codes){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-overview-of-status-codes}

The status codes listed below are defined in this specification. The
reason phrases listed here are only recommendations \-- they can be
replaced by local equivalents or left out altogether without affecting
the protocol.[¶](#section-15.1-1){.pilcrow}

Responses with status codes that are defined as heuristically cacheable
(e.g., 200, 203, 204, 206, 300, 301, 308, 404, 405, 410, 414, and 501 in
this specification) can be reused by a cache with heuristic expiration
unless otherwise indicated by the method definition or explicit cache
controls \[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]; all other status codes are not
heuristically cacheable.[¶](#section-15.1-2){.pilcrow}

Additional status codes, outside the scope of this specification, have
been specified for use in HTTP. All such status codes ought to be
registered within the \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) Status Code
Registry\", as described in [Section
16.2](#status.code.extensibility){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.1xx}
::: {#section-15.2 .section}
### [15.2.](#section-15.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Informational 1xx](#name-informational-1xx){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-informational-1xx}

[]{#iref-1xx-informational-status-co .iref}
[]{#iref-status-codes-classes-1xx-in .iref}

The 1xx (Informational) class of status code indicates an interim
response for communicating connection status or request progress prior
to completing the requested action and sending a final response. Since
HTTP/1.0 did not define any 1xx status codes, a server [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} send a 1xx response to an HTTP/1.0
client.[¶](#section-15.2-1){.pilcrow}

A 1xx response is terminated by the end of the header section; it cannot
contain content or trailers.[¶](#section-15.2-2){.pilcrow}

A client [MUST]{.bcp14} be able to parse one or more 1xx responses
received prior to a final response, even if the client does not expect
one. A user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} ignore unexpected 1xx
responses.[¶](#section-15.2-3){.pilcrow}

A proxy [MUST]{.bcp14} forward 1xx responses unless the proxy itself
requested the generation of the 1xx response. For example, if a proxy
adds an \"Expect: 100-continue\" header field when it forwards a
request, then it need not forward the corresponding [100
(Continue)](#status.100){.xref}
response(s).[¶](#section-15.2-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#status.100}
::: {#section-15.2.1 .section}
#### [15.2.1.](#section-15.2.1){.section-number .selfRef} [100 Continue](#name-100-continue){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-100-continue}

[]{#iref-100-continue-status-code-40 .iref}

The 100 (Continue) status code indicates that the initial part of a
request has been received and has not yet been rejected by the server.
The server intends to send a final response after the request has been
fully received and acted upon.[¶](#section-15.2.1-1){.pilcrow}

When the request contains an [Expect](#field.expect){.xref} header field
that includes a [100-continue](#field.expect){.xref} expectation, the
100 response indicates that the server wishes to receive the request
content, as described in [Section 10.1.1](#field.expect){.xref}. The
client ought to continue sending the request and discard the 100
response.[¶](#section-15.2.1-2){.pilcrow}

If the request did not contain an [Expect](#field.expect){.xref} header
field containing the [100-continue](#field.expect){.xref} expectation,
the client can simply discard this interim
response.[¶](#section-15.2.1-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.101}
::: {#section-15.2.2 .section}
#### [15.2.2.](#section-15.2.2){.section-number .selfRef} [101 Switching Protocols](#name-101-switching-protocols){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-101-switching-protocols}

[]{#iref-101-switching-protocols-sta .iref}

The 101 (Switching Protocols) status code indicates that the server
understands and is willing to comply with the client\'s request, via the
[Upgrade](#field.upgrade){.xref} header field ([Section
7.8](#field.upgrade){.xref}), for a change in the application protocol
being used on this connection. The server [MUST]{.bcp14} generate an
Upgrade header field in the response that indicates which protocol(s)
will be in effect after this response.[¶](#section-15.2.2-1){.pilcrow}

It is assumed that the server will only agree to switch protocols when
it is advantageous to do so. For example, switching to a newer version
of HTTP might be advantageous over older versions, and switching to a
real-time, synchronous protocol might be advantageous when delivering
resources that use such features.[¶](#section-15.2.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#status.2xx}
::: {#section-15.3 .section}
### [15.3.](#section-15.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Successful 2xx](#name-successful-2xx){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-successful-2xx}

[]{#iref-2xx-successful-status-code- .iref}
[]{#iref-status-codes-classes-2xx-su .iref}

The 2xx (Successful) class of status code indicates that the client\'s
request was successfully received, understood, and
accepted.[¶](#section-15.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#status.200}
::: {#section-15.3.1 .section}
#### [15.3.1.](#section-15.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [200 OK](#name-200-ok){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-200-ok}

[]{#iref-200-ok-status-code-404 .iref}

The 200 (OK) status code indicates that the request has succeeded. The
content sent in a 200 response depends on the request method. For the
methods defined by this specification, the intended meaning of the
content can be summarized as:[¶](#section-15.3.1-1){.pilcrow}

  Request Method   Response content is a representation of:
  ---------------- ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
  GET              the [target resource](#target.resource){.xref}
  HEAD             the [target resource](#target.resource){.xref}, like GET, but without transferring the representation data
  POST             the status of, or results obtained from, the action
  PUT, DELETE      the status of the action
  OPTIONS          communication options for the target resource
  TRACE            the request message as received by the server returning the trace

  : [Table 6](#table-6){.selfRef}

Aside from responses to CONNECT, a 200 response is expected to contain
message content unless the message framing explicitly indicates that the
content has zero length. If some aspect of the request indicates a
preference for no content upon success, the origin server ought to send
a 204 (No Content) response instead. For CONNECT, there is no content
because the successful result is a tunnel, which begins immediately
after the 200 response header section.[¶](#section-15.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

A 200 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

In 200 responses to GET or HEAD, an origin server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send
any available validator fields ([Section
8.8](#response.validator){.xref}) for the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}, with both a strong
entity tag and a [Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} date being
preferred.[¶](#section-15.3.1-5){.pilcrow}

In 200 responses to state-changing methods, any validator fields
([Section 8.8](#response.validator){.xref}) sent in the response convey
the current validators for the new representation formed as a result of
successfully applying the request semantics. Note that the PUT method
([Section 9.3.4](#PUT){.xref}) has additional requirements that might
preclude sending such validators.[¶](#section-15.3.1-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.201}
::: {#section-15.3.2 .section}
#### [15.3.2.](#section-15.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [201 Created](#name-201-created){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-201-created}

[]{#iref-201-created-status-code-405 .iref}

The 201 (Created) status code indicates that the request has been
fulfilled and has resulted in one or more new resources being created.
The primary resource created by the request is identified by either a
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field in the response or, if
no [Location](#field.location){.xref} header field is received, by the
target URI.[¶](#section-15.3.2-1){.pilcrow}

The 201 response content typically describes and links to the
resource(s) created. Any validator fields ([Section
8.8](#response.validator){.xref}) sent in the response convey the
current validators for a new representation created by the request. Note
that the PUT method ([Section 9.3.4](#PUT){.xref}) has additional
requirements that might preclude sending such
validators.[¶](#section-15.3.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.202}
::: {#section-15.3.3 .section}
#### [15.3.3.](#section-15.3.3){.section-number .selfRef} [202 Accepted](#name-202-accepted){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-202-accepted}

[]{#iref-202-accepted-status-code-40 .iref}

The 202 (Accepted) status code indicates that the request has been
accepted for processing, but the processing has not been completed. The
request might or might not eventually be acted upon, as it might be
disallowed when processing actually takes place. There is no facility in
HTTP for re-sending a status code from an asynchronous
operation.[¶](#section-15.3.3-1){.pilcrow}

The 202 response is intentionally noncommittal. Its purpose is to allow
a server to accept a request for some other process (perhaps a
batch-oriented process that is only run once per day) without requiring
that the user agent\'s connection to the server persist until the
process is completed. The representation sent with this response ought
to describe the request\'s current status and point to (or embed) a
status monitor that can provide the user with an estimate of when the
request will be fulfilled.[¶](#section-15.3.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.203}
::: {#section-15.3.4 .section}
#### [15.3.4.](#section-15.3.4){.section-number .selfRef} [203 Non-Authoritative Information](#name-203-non-authoritative-infor){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-203-non-authoritative-infor}

[]{#iref-203-non-authoritative-infor .iref}

The 203 (Non-Authoritative Information) status code indicates that the
request was successful but the enclosed content has been modified from
that of the origin server\'s [200 (OK)](#status.200){.xref} response by
a transforming proxy ([Section 7.7](#message.transformations){.xref}).
This status code allows the proxy to notify recipients when a
transformation has been applied, since that knowledge might impact later
decisions regarding the content. For example, future cache validation
requests for the content might only be applicable along the same request
path (through the same proxies).[¶](#section-15.3.4-1){.pilcrow}

A 203 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.3.4-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.204}
::: {#section-15.3.5 .section}
#### [15.3.5.](#section-15.3.5){.section-number .selfRef} [204 No Content](#name-204-no-content){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-204-no-content}

[]{#iref-204-no-content-status-code- .iref}

The 204 (No Content) status code indicates that the server has
successfully fulfilled the request and that there is no additional
content to send in the response content. Metadata in the response header
fields refer to the [target resource](#target.resource){.xref} and its
[selected representation](#selected.representation){.xref} after the
requested action was applied.[¶](#section-15.3.5-1){.pilcrow}

For example, if a 204 status code is received in response to a PUT
request and the response contains an [ETag](#field.etag){.xref} field,
then the PUT was successful and the ETag field value contains the entity
tag for the new representation of that target
resource.[¶](#section-15.3.5-2){.pilcrow}

The 204 response allows a server to indicate that the action has been
successfully applied to the target resource, while implying that the
user agent does not need to traverse away from its current \"document
view\" (if any). The server assumes that the user agent will provide
some indication of the success to its user, in accord with its own
interface, and apply any new or updated metadata in the response to its
active representation.[¶](#section-15.3.5-3){.pilcrow}

For example, a 204 status code is commonly used with document editing
interfaces corresponding to a \"save\" action, such that the document
being saved remains available to the user for editing. It is also
frequently used with interfaces that expect automated data transfers to
be prevalent, such as within distributed version control
systems.[¶](#section-15.3.5-4){.pilcrow}

A 204 response is terminated by the end of the header section; it cannot
contain content or trailers.[¶](#section-15.3.5-5){.pilcrow}

A 204 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.3.5-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.205}
::: {#section-15.3.6 .section}
#### [15.3.6.](#section-15.3.6){.section-number .selfRef} [205 Reset Content](#name-205-reset-content){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-205-reset-content}

[]{#iref-205-reset-content-status-co .iref}

The 205 (Reset Content) status code indicates that the server has
fulfilled the request and desires that the user agent reset the
\"document view\", which caused the request to be sent, to its original
state as received from the origin
server.[¶](#section-15.3.6-1){.pilcrow}

This response is intended to support a common data entry use case where
the user receives content that supports data entry (a form, notepad,
canvas, etc.), enters or manipulates data in that space, causes the
entered data to be submitted in a request, and then the data entry
mechanism is reset for the next entry so that the user can easily
initiate another input action.[¶](#section-15.3.6-2){.pilcrow}

Since the 205 status code implies that no additional content will be
provided, a server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} generate content in a 205
response.[¶](#section-15.3.6-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.206}
::: {#section-15.3.7 .section}
#### [15.3.7.](#section-15.3.7){.section-number .selfRef} [206 Partial Content](#name-206-partial-content){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-206-partial-content}

[]{#iref-206-partial-content-status- .iref}

The 206 (Partial Content) status code indicates that the server is
successfully fulfilling a range request for the target resource by
transferring one or more parts of the [selected
representation](#selected.representation){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.3.7-1){.pilcrow}

A server that supports range requests ([Section
14](#range.requests){.xref}) will usually attempt to satisfy all of the
requested ranges, since sending less data will likely result in another
client request for the remainder. However, a server might want to send
only a subset of the data requested for reasons of its own, such as
temporary unavailability, cache efficiency, load balancing, etc. Since a
206 response is self-descriptive, the client can still understand a
response that only partially satisfies its range
request.[¶](#section-15.3.7-2){.pilcrow}

A client [MUST]{.bcp14} inspect a 206 response\'s
[Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref} and
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} field(s) to determine what
parts are enclosed and whether additional requests are
needed.[¶](#section-15.3.7-3){.pilcrow}

A server that generates a 206 response [MUST]{.bcp14} generate the
following header fields, in addition to those required in the
subsections below, if the field would have been sent in a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response to the same request:
[Date](#field.date){.xref}, Cache-Control, [ETag](#field.etag){.xref},
Expires, [Content-Location](#field.content-location){.xref}, and
[Vary](#field.vary){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.3.7-4){.pilcrow}

A [Content-Length](#field.content-length){.xref} header field present in
a 206 response indicates the number of octets in the content of this
message, which is usually not the complete length of the selected
representation. Each [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header
field includes information about the selected representation\'s complete
length.[¶](#section-15.3.7-5){.pilcrow}

A sender that generates a 206 response to a request with an
[If-Range](#field.if-range){.xref} header field [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14}
generate other representation header fields beyond those required
because the client already has a prior response containing those header
fields. Otherwise, a sender [MUST]{.bcp14} generate all of the
representation header fields that would have been sent in a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response to the same
request.[¶](#section-15.3.7-6){.pilcrow}

A 206 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by explicit cache controls (see [Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.3.7-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#partial.single}
::: {#section-15.3.7.1 .section}
##### [15.3.7.1.](#section-15.3.7.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Single Part](#name-single-part){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-single-part}

If a single part is being transferred, the server generating the 206
response [MUST]{.bcp14} generate a
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field, describing
what range of the selected representation is enclosed, and a content
consisting of the range. For example:[¶](#section-15.3.7.1-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-15.3.7.1-2}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
HTTP/1.1 206 Partial Content
Date: Wed, 15 Nov 1995 06:25:24 GMT
Last-Modified: Wed, 15 Nov 1995 04:58:08 GMT
Content-Range: bytes 21010-47021/47022
Content-Length: 26012
Content-Type: image/gif

... 26012 bytes of partial image data ...
```

[¶](#section-15.3.7.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#partial.multipart}
::: {#section-15.3.7.2 .section}
##### [15.3.7.2.](#section-15.3.7.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Multiple Parts](#name-multiple-parts){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-multiple-parts}

If multiple parts are being transferred, the server generating the 206
response [MUST]{.bcp14} generate \"multipart/byteranges\" content, as
defined in [Section 14.6](#multipart.byteranges){.xref}, and a
[Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref} header field containing the
\"multipart/byteranges\" media type and its required boundary parameter.
To avoid confusion with single-part responses, a server [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} generate a [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref}
header field in the HTTP header section of a multiple part response
(this field will be sent in each part
instead).[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-1){.pilcrow}

Within the header area of each body part in the multipart content, the
server [MUST]{.bcp14} generate a
[Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field corresponding
to the range being enclosed in that body part. If the selected
representation would have had a
[Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref} header field in a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate
that same [Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref} header field in the
header area of each body part. For
example:[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-15.3.7.2-3}
``` {.lang-http-message .sourcecode}
HTTP/1.1 206 Partial Content
Date: Wed, 15 Nov 1995 06:25:24 GMT
Last-Modified: Wed, 15 Nov 1995 04:58:08 GMT
Content-Length: 1741
Content-Type: multipart/byteranges; boundary=THIS_STRING_SEPARATES

--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES
Content-Type: application/pdf
Content-Range: bytes 500-999/8000

...the first range...
--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES
Content-Type: application/pdf
Content-Range: bytes 7000-7999/8000

...the second range
--THIS_STRING_SEPARATES--
```

[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::

When multiple ranges are requested, a server [MAY]{.bcp14} coalesce any
of the ranges that overlap, or that are separated by a gap that is
smaller than the overhead of sending multiple parts, regardless of the
order in which the corresponding range-spec appeared in the received
[Range](#field.range){.xref} header field. Since the typical overhead
between each part of a \"multipart/byteranges\" is around 80 bytes,
depending on the selected representation\'s media type and the chosen
boundary parameter length, it can be less efficient to transfer many
small disjoint parts than it is to transfer the entire selected
representation.[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-4){.pilcrow}

A server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} generate a multipart response to a request
for a single range, since a client that does not request multiple parts
might not support multipart responses. However, a server [MAY]{.bcp14}
generate a \"multipart/byteranges\" response with only a single body
part if multiple ranges were requested and only one range was found to
be satisfiable or only one range remained after coalescing. A client
that cannot process a \"multipart/byteranges\" response [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} generate a request that asks for multiple
ranges.[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-5){.pilcrow}

A server that generates a multipart response [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send the
parts in the same order that the corresponding range-spec appeared in
the received [Range](#field.range){.xref} header field, excluding those
ranges that were deemed unsatisfiable or that were coalesced into other
ranges. A client that receives a multipart response [MUST]{.bcp14}
inspect the [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field
present in each body part in order to determine which range is contained
in that body part; a client cannot rely on receiving the same ranges
that it requested, nor the same order that it
requested.[¶](#section-15.3.7.2-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#combining.byte.ranges}
::: {#section-15.3.7.3 .section}
##### [15.3.7.3.](#section-15.3.7.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Combining Parts](#name-combining-parts){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-combining-parts}

A response might transfer only a subrange of a representation if the
connection closed prematurely or if the request used one or more Range
specifications. After several such transfers, a client might have
received several ranges of the same representation. These ranges can
only be safely combined if they all have in common the same strong
validator ([Section
8.8.1](#weak.and.strong.validators){.xref}).[¶](#section-15.3.7.3-1){.pilcrow}

A client that has received multiple partial responses to GET requests on
a target resource [MAY]{.bcp14} combine those responses into a larger
continuous range if they share the same strong
validator.[¶](#section-15.3.7.3-2){.pilcrow}

If the most recent response is an incomplete [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response, then the header fields of that
response are used for any combined response and replace those of the
matching stored responses.[¶](#section-15.3.7.3-3){.pilcrow}

If the most recent response is a [206 (Partial
Content)](#status.206){.xref} response and at least one of the matching
stored responses is a [200 (OK)](#status.200){.xref}, then the combined
response header fields consist of the most recent 200 response\'s header
fields. If all of the matching stored responses are 206 responses, then
the stored response with the most recent header fields is used as the
source of header fields for the combined response, except that the
client [MUST]{.bcp14} use other header fields provided in the new
response, aside from [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref}, to
replace all instances of the corresponding header fields in the stored
response.[¶](#section-15.3.7.3-4){.pilcrow}

The combined response content consists of the union of partial content
ranges within the new response and all of the matching stored responses.
If the union consists of the entire range of the representation, then
the client [MUST]{.bcp14} process the combined response as if it were a
complete [200 (OK)](#status.200){.xref} response, including a
[Content-Length](#field.content-length){.xref} header field that
reflects the complete length. Otherwise, the client [MUST]{.bcp14}
process the set of continuous ranges as one of the following: an
incomplete [200 (OK)](#status.200){.xref} response if the combined
response is a prefix of the representation, a single [206 (Partial
Content)](#status.206){.xref} response containing
\"multipart/byteranges\" content, or multiple [206 (Partial
Content)](#status.206){.xref} responses, each with one continuous range
that is indicated by a [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref}
header field.[¶](#section-15.3.7.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#status.3xx}
::: {#section-15.4 .section}
### [15.4.](#section-15.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Redirection 3xx](#name-redirection-3xx){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-redirection-3xx}

[]{#iref-3xx-redirection-status-code .iref}
[]{#iref-status-codes-classes-3xx-re .iref}

The 3xx (Redirection) class of status code indicates that further action
needs to be taken by the user agent in order to fulfill the request.
There are several types of redirects:[¶](#section-15.4-1){.pilcrow}

1.  [Redirects that indicate this resource might be available at a
    different URI, as provided by the [Location](#field.location){.xref}
    header field, as in the status codes [301 (Moved
    Permanently)](#status.301){.xref}, [302
    (Found)](#status.302){.xref}, [307 (Temporary
    Redirect)](#status.307){.xref}, and [308 (Permanent
    Redirect)](#status.308){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.4-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-2.1}
2.  [Redirection that offers a choice among matching resources capable
    of representing this resource, as in the [300 (Multiple
    Choices)](#status.300){.xref} status
    code.[¶](#section-15.4-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-2.2}
3.  [Redirection to a different resource, identified by the
    [Location](#field.location){.xref} header field, that can represent
    an indirect response to the request, as in the [303 (See
    Other)](#status.303){.xref} status
    code.[¶](#section-15.4-2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-2.3}
4.  [Redirection to a previously stored result, as in the [304 (Not
    Modified)](#status.304){.xref} status
    code.[¶](#section-15.4-2.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-2.4}

**Note:** In HTTP/1.0, the status codes [301 (Moved
Permanently)](#status.301){.xref} and [302 (Found)](#status.302){.xref}
were originally defined as method-preserving
(\[[HTTP/1.0](#HTTP10){.xref}\], [Section
9.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc1945#section-9.3){.relref}) to
match their implementation at CERN; [303 (See
Other)](#status.303){.xref} was defined for a redirection that changed
its method to GET. However, early user agents split on whether to
redirect POST requests as POST (according to then-current specification)
or as GET (the safer alternative when redirected to a different site).
Prevailing practice eventually converged on changing the method to GET.
[307 (Temporary Redirect)](#status.307){.xref} and [308 (Permanent
Redirect)](#status.308){.xref} \[[RFC7538](#RFC7538){.xref}\] were later
added to unambiguously indicate method-preserving redirects, and status
codes [301](#status.301){.xref} and [302](#status.302){.xref} have been
adjusted to allow a POST request to be redirected as
GET.[¶](#section-15.4-3.1){.pilcrow}

If a [Location](#field.location){.xref} header field ([Section
10.2.2](#field.location){.xref}) is provided, the user agent
[MAY]{.bcp14} automatically redirect its request to the URI referenced
by the Location field value, even if the specific status code is not
understood. Automatic redirection needs to be done with care for methods
not known to be [safe](#safe.methods){.xref}, as defined in [Section
9.2.1](#safe.methods){.xref}, since the user might not wish to redirect
an unsafe request.[¶](#section-15.4-4){.pilcrow}

When automatically following a redirected request, the user agent
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} resend the original request message with the following
modifications:[¶](#section-15.4-5){.pilcrow}

1.  ::: {#section-15.4-6.1}
    Replace the target URI with the URI referenced by the redirection
    response\'s [Location](#field.location){.xref} header field value
    after resolving it relative to the original request\'s target
    URI.[¶](#section-15.4-6.1.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

2.  ::: {#section-15.4-6.2}
    Remove header fields that were automatically generated by the
    implementation, replacing them with updated values as appropriate to
    the new request. This includes:[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

    1.  [Connection-specific header fields (see [Section
        7.6.1](#field.connection){.xref}),[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-6.2.2.1}
    2.  [Header fields specific to the client\'s proxy configuration,
        including (but not limited to)
        [Proxy-Authorization](#field.proxy-authorization){.xref},[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-6.2.2.2}
    3.  [Origin-specific header fields (if any), including (but not
        limited to)
        [Host](#field.host){.xref},[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.2.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-6.2.2.3}
    4.  [Validating header fields that were added by the
        implementation\'s cache (e.g.,
        [If-None-Match](#field.if-none-match){.xref},
        [If-Modified-Since](#field.if-modified-since){.xref}),
        and[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.2.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-6.2.2.4}
    5.  [Resource-specific header fields, including (but not limited to)
        [Referer](#field.referer){.xref}, Origin,
        [Authorization](#field.authorization){.xref}, and
        Cookie.[¶](#section-15.4-6.2.2.5){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4-6.2.2.5}
    :::

3.  ::: {#section-15.4-6.3}
    Consider removing header fields that were not automatically
    generated by the implementation (i.e., those present in the request
    because they were added by the calling context) where there are
    security implications; this includes but is not limited to
    [Authorization](#field.authorization){.xref} and
    Cookie.[¶](#section-15.4-6.3.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

4.  ::: {#section-15.4-6.4}
    Change the request method according to the redirecting status
    code\'s semantics, if applicable.[¶](#section-15.4-6.4.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

5.  ::: {#section-15.4-6.5}
    If the request method has been changed to GET or HEAD, remove
    content-specific header fields, including (but not limited to)
    [Content-Encoding](#field.content-encoding){.xref},
    [Content-Language](#field.content-language){.xref},
    [Content-Location](#field.content-location){.xref},
    [Content-Type](#field.content-type){.xref},
    [Content-Length](#field.content-length){.xref}, Digest,
    [Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.4-6.5.1){.pilcrow}
    :::

A client [SHOULD]{.bcp14} detect and intervene in cyclical redirections
(i.e., \"infinite\" redirection loops).[¶](#section-15.4-7){.pilcrow}

**Note:** An earlier version of this specification recommended a maximum
of five redirections (\[[RFC2068](#RFC2068){.xref}\], [Section
10.3](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2068#section-10.3){.relref}).
Content developers need to be aware that some clients might implement
such a fixed limitation.[¶](#section-15.4-8.1){.pilcrow}

::: {#status.300}
::: {#section-15.4.1 .section}
#### [15.4.1.](#section-15.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [300 Multiple Choices](#name-300-multiple-choices){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-300-multiple-choices}

[]{#iref-300-multiple-choices-status .iref}

The 300 (Multiple Choices) status code indicates that the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} has more than one representation,
each with its own more specific identifier, and information about the
alternatives is being provided so that the user (or user agent) can
select a preferred representation by redirecting its request to one or
more of those identifiers. In other words, the server desires that the
user agent engage in reactive negotiation to select the most appropriate
representation(s) for its needs ([Section
12](#content.negotiation){.xref}).[¶](#section-15.4.1-1){.pilcrow}

If the server has a preferred choice, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
generate a [Location](#field.location){.xref} header field containing a
preferred choice\'s URI reference. The user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} use the
Location field value for automatic
redirection.[¶](#section-15.4.1-2){.pilcrow}

For request methods other than HEAD, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
generate content in the 300 response containing a list of representation
metadata and URI reference(s) from which the user or user agent can
choose the one most preferred. The user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} make a
selection from that list automatically if it understands the provided
media type. A specific format for automatic selection is not defined by
this specification because HTTP tries to remain orthogonal to the
definition of its content. In practice, the representation is provided
in some easily parsed format believed to be acceptable to the user
agent, as determined by shared design or content negotiation, or in some
commonly accepted hypertext format.[¶](#section-15.4.1-3){.pilcrow}

A 300 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.4.1-4){.pilcrow}

**Note:** The original proposal for the 300 status code defined the URI
header field as providing a list of alternative representations, such
that it would be usable for 200, 300, and 406 responses and be
transferred in responses to the HEAD method. However, lack of deployment
and disagreement over syntax led to both URI and Alternates (a
subsequent proposal) being dropped from this specification. It is
possible to communicate the list as a Link header field value
\[[RFC8288](#RFC8288){.xref}\] whose members have a relationship of
\"alternate\", though deployment is a chicken-and-egg
problem.[¶](#section-15.4.1-5.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.301}
::: {#section-15.4.2 .section}
#### [15.4.2.](#section-15.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [301 Moved Permanently](#name-301-moved-permanently){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-301-moved-permanently}

[]{#iref-301-moved-permanently-statu .iref}

The 301 (Moved Permanently) status code indicates that the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} has been assigned a new permanent URI
and any future references to this resource ought to use one of the
enclosed URIs. The server is suggesting that a user agent with
link-editing capability can permanently replace references to the target
URI with one of the new references sent by the server. However, this
suggestion is usually ignored unless the user agent is actively editing
references (e.g., engaged in authoring content), the connection is
secured, and the origin server is a trusted authority for the content
being edited.[¶](#section-15.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field in the response
containing a preferred URI reference for the new permanent URI. The user
agent [MAY]{.bcp14} use the Location field value for automatic
redirection. The server\'s response content usually contains a short
hypertext note with a hyperlink to the new
URI(s).[¶](#section-15.4.2-2){.pilcrow}

**Note:** For historical reasons, a user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} change the
request method from POST to GET for the subsequent request. If this
behavior is undesired, the [308 (Permanent
Redirect)](#status.308){.xref} status code can be used
instead.[¶](#section-15.4.2-3.1){.pilcrow}

A 301 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.4.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.302}
::: {#section-15.4.3 .section}
#### [15.4.3.](#section-15.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [302 Found](#name-302-found){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-302-found}

[]{#iref-302-found-status-code-415 .iref}

The 302 (Found) status code indicates that the target resource resides
temporarily under a different URI. Since the redirection might be
altered on occasion, the client ought to continue to use the target URI
for future requests.[¶](#section-15.4.3-1){.pilcrow}

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field in the response
containing a URI reference for the different URI. The user agent
[MAY]{.bcp14} use the Location field value for automatic redirection.
The server\'s response content usually contains a short hypertext note
with a hyperlink to the different
URI(s).[¶](#section-15.4.3-2){.pilcrow}

**Note:** For historical reasons, a user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} change the
request method from POST to GET for the subsequent request. If this
behavior is undesired, the [307 (Temporary
Redirect)](#status.307){.xref} status code can be used
instead.[¶](#section-15.4.3-3.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.303}
::: {#section-15.4.4 .section}
#### [15.4.4.](#section-15.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [303 See Other](#name-303-see-other){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-303-see-other}

[]{#iref-303-see-other-status-code-4 .iref}

The 303 (See Other) status code indicates that the server is redirecting
the user agent to a different resource, as indicated by a URI in the
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field, which is intended to
provide an indirect response to the original request. A user agent can
perform a retrieval request targeting that URI (a GET or HEAD request if
using HTTP), which might also be redirected, and present the eventual
result as an answer to the original request. Note that the new URI in
the Location header field is not considered equivalent to the target
URI.[¶](#section-15.4.4-1){.pilcrow}

This status code is applicable to any HTTP method. It is primarily used
to allow the output of a POST action to redirect the user agent to a
different resource, since doing so provides the information
corresponding to the POST response as a resource that can be separately
identified, bookmarked, and cached.[¶](#section-15.4.4-2){.pilcrow}

A 303 response to a GET request indicates that the origin server does
not have a representation of the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} that can be transferred by the server
over HTTP. However, the [Location](#field.location){.xref} field value
refers to a resource that is descriptive of the target resource, such
that making a retrieval request on that other resource might result in a
representation that is useful to recipients without implying that it
represents the original target resource. Note that answers to the
questions of what can be represented, what representations are adequate,
and what might be a useful description are outside the scope of
HTTP.[¶](#section-15.4.4-3){.pilcrow}

Except for responses to a HEAD request, the representation of a 303
response ought to contain a short hypertext note with a hyperlink to the
same URI reference provided in the [Location](#field.location){.xref}
header field.[¶](#section-15.4.4-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.304}
::: {#section-15.4.5 .section}
#### [15.4.5.](#section-15.4.5){.section-number .selfRef} [304 Not Modified](#name-304-not-modified){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-304-not-modified}

[]{#iref-304-not-modified-status-cod .iref}

The 304 (Not Modified) status code indicates that a conditional GET or
HEAD request has been received and would have resulted in a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response if it were not for the fact that the
condition evaluated to false. In other words, there is no need for the
server to transfer a representation of the target resource because the
request indicates that the client, which made the request conditional,
already has a valid representation; the server is therefore redirecting
the client to make use of that stored representation as if it were the
content of a [200 (OK)](#status.200){.xref}
response.[¶](#section-15.4.5-1){.pilcrow}

The server generating a 304 response [MUST]{.bcp14} generate any of the
following header fields that would have been sent in a [200
(OK)](#status.200){.xref} response to the same
request:[¶](#section-15.4.5-2){.pilcrow}

-   [[Content-Location](#field.content-location){.xref},
    [Date](#field.date){.xref}, [ETag](#field.etag){.xref}, and
    [Vary](#field.vary){.xref}[¶](#section-15.4.5-3.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4.5-3.1}
-   [Cache-Control and Expires (see
    \[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\])[¶](#section-15.4.5-3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-15.4.5-3.2}

Since the goal of a 304 response is to minimize information transfer
when the recipient already has one or more cached representations, a
sender [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} generate representation metadata other than
the above listed fields unless said metadata exists for the purpose of
guiding cache updates (e.g.,
[Last-Modified](#field.last-modified){.xref} might be useful if the
response does not have an [ETag](#field.etag){.xref}
field).[¶](#section-15.4.5-4){.pilcrow}

Requirements on a cache that receives a 304 response are defined in
[Section
4.3.4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.3.4){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]. If the conditional request originated
with an outbound client, such as a user agent with its own cache sending
a conditional GET to a shared proxy, then the proxy [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
forward the 304 response to that client.[¶](#section-15.4.5-5){.pilcrow}

A 304 response is terminated by the end of the header section; it cannot
contain content or trailers.[¶](#section-15.4.5-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.305}
::: {#section-15.4.6 .section}
#### [15.4.6.](#section-15.4.6){.section-number .selfRef} [305 Use Proxy](#name-305-use-proxy){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-305-use-proxy}

[]{#iref-305-use-proxy-status-code-4 .iref}

The 305 (Use Proxy) status code was defined in a previous version of
this specification and is now deprecated ([Appendix
B](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#appendix-B){.relref} of
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.4.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.306}
::: {#section-15.4.7 .section}
#### [15.4.7.](#section-15.4.7){.section-number .selfRef} [306 (Unused)](#name-306-unused){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-306-unused}

[]{#iref-306-unused-status-code-419 .iref}

The 306 status code was defined in a previous version of this
specification, is no longer used, and the code is
reserved.[¶](#section-15.4.7-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.307}
::: {#section-15.4.8 .section}
#### [15.4.8.](#section-15.4.8){.section-number .selfRef} [307 Temporary Redirect](#name-307-temporary-redirect){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-307-temporary-redirect}

[]{#iref-307-temporary-redirect-stat .iref}

The 307 (Temporary Redirect) status code indicates that the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} resides temporarily under a different
URI and the user agent [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} change the request method if
it performs an automatic redirection to that URI. Since the redirection
can change over time, the client ought to continue using the original
target URI for future requests.[¶](#section-15.4.8-1){.pilcrow}

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field in the response
containing a URI reference for the different URI. The user agent
[MAY]{.bcp14} use the Location field value for automatic redirection.
The server\'s response content usually contains a short hypertext note
with a hyperlink to the different
URI(s).[¶](#section-15.4.8-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.308}
::: {#section-15.4.9 .section}
#### [15.4.9.](#section-15.4.9){.section-number .selfRef} [308 Permanent Redirect](#name-308-permanent-redirect){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-308-permanent-redirect}

[]{#iref-308-permanent-redirect-stat .iref}

The 308 (Permanent Redirect) status code indicates that the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} has been assigned a new permanent URI
and any future references to this resource ought to use one of the
enclosed URIs. The server is suggesting that a user agent with
link-editing capability can permanently replace references to the target
URI with one of the new references sent by the server. However, this
suggestion is usually ignored unless the user agent is actively editing
references (e.g., engaged in authoring content), the connection is
secured, and the origin server is a trusted authority for the content
being edited.[¶](#section-15.4.9-1){.pilcrow}

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate a
[Location](#field.location){.xref} header field in the response
containing a preferred URI reference for the new permanent URI. The user
agent [MAY]{.bcp14} use the Location field value for automatic
redirection. The server\'s response content usually contains a short
hypertext note with a hyperlink to the new
URI(s).[¶](#section-15.4.9-2){.pilcrow}

A 308 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.4.9-3){.pilcrow}

**Note:** This status code is much younger (June 2014) than its sibling
codes and thus might not be recognized everywhere. See [Section
4](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7538#section-4){.relref} of
\[[RFC7538](#RFC7538){.xref}\] for deployment
considerations.[¶](#section-15.4.9-4.1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#status.4xx}
::: {#section-15.5 .section}
### [15.5.](#section-15.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Client Error 4xx](#name-client-error-4xx){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-client-error-4xx}

[]{#iref-4xx-client-error-status-cod .iref}
[]{#iref-status-codes-classes-4xx-cl .iref}

The 4xx (Client Error) class of status code indicates that the client
seems to have erred. Except when responding to a HEAD request, the
server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} send a representation containing an explanation
of the error situation, and whether it is a temporary or permanent
condition. These status codes are applicable to any request method. User
agents [SHOULD]{.bcp14} display any included representation to the
user.[¶](#section-15.5-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#status.400}
::: {#section-15.5.1 .section}
#### [15.5.1.](#section-15.5.1){.section-number .selfRef} [400 Bad Request](#name-400-bad-request){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-400-bad-request}

[]{#iref-400-bad-request-status-code .iref}

The 400 (Bad Request) status code indicates that the server cannot or
will not process the request due to something that is perceived to be a
client error (e.g., malformed request syntax, invalid request message
framing, or deceptive request routing).[¶](#section-15.5.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.401}
::: {#section-15.5.2 .section}
#### [15.5.2.](#section-15.5.2){.section-number .selfRef} [401 Unauthorized](#name-401-unauthorized){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-401-unauthorized}

[]{#iref-401-unauthorized-status-cod .iref}

The 401 (Unauthorized) status code indicates that the request has not
been applied because it lacks valid authentication credentials for the
target resource. The server generating a 401 response [MUST]{.bcp14}
send a [WWW-Authenticate](#field.www-authenticate){.xref} header field
([Section 11.6.1](#field.www-authenticate){.xref}) containing at least
one challenge applicable to the target
resource.[¶](#section-15.5.2-1){.pilcrow}

If the request included authentication credentials, then the 401
response indicates that authorization has been refused for those
credentials. The user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} repeat the request with a new
or replaced [Authorization](#field.authorization){.xref} header field
([Section 11.6.2](#field.authorization){.xref}). If the 401 response
contains the same challenge as the prior response, and the user agent
has already attempted authentication at least once, then the user agent
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} present the enclosed representation to the user, since
it usually contains relevant diagnostic
information.[¶](#section-15.5.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.402}
::: {#section-15.5.3 .section}
#### [15.5.3.](#section-15.5.3){.section-number .selfRef} [402 Payment Required](#name-402-payment-required){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-402-payment-required}

[]{#iref-402-payment-required-status .iref}

The 402 (Payment Required) status code is reserved for future
use.[¶](#section-15.5.3-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.403}
::: {#section-15.5.4 .section}
#### [15.5.4.](#section-15.5.4){.section-number .selfRef} [403 Forbidden](#name-403-forbidden){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-403-forbidden}

[]{#iref-403-forbidden-status-code-4 .iref}

The 403 (Forbidden) status code indicates that the server understood the
request but refuses to fulfill it. A server that wishes to make public
why the request has been forbidden can describe that reason in the
response content (if any).[¶](#section-15.5.4-1){.pilcrow}

If authentication credentials were provided in the request, the server
considers them insufficient to grant access. The client [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} automatically repeat the request with the same credentials.
The client [MAY]{.bcp14} repeat the request with new or different
credentials. However, a request might be forbidden for reasons unrelated
to the credentials.[¶](#section-15.5.4-2){.pilcrow}

An origin server that wishes to \"hide\" the current existence of a
forbidden [target resource](#target.resource){.xref} [MAY]{.bcp14}
instead respond with a status code of [404 (Not
Found)](#status.404){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.5.4-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.404}
::: {#section-15.5.5 .section}
#### [15.5.5.](#section-15.5.5){.section-number .selfRef} [404 Not Found](#name-404-not-found){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-404-not-found}

[]{#iref-404-not-found-status-code-4 .iref}

The 404 (Not Found) status code indicates that the origin server did not
find a current representation for the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} or is not willing to disclose that
one exists. A 404 status code does not indicate whether this lack of
representation is temporary or permanent; the [410
(Gone)](#status.410){.xref} status code is preferred over 404 if the
origin server knows, presumably through some configurable means, that
the condition is likely to be permanent.[¶](#section-15.5.5-1){.pilcrow}

A 404 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.5.5-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.405}
::: {#section-15.5.6 .section}
#### [15.5.6.](#section-15.5.6){.section-number .selfRef} [405 Method Not Allowed](#name-405-method-not-allowed){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-405-method-not-allowed}

[]{#iref-405-method-not-allowed-stat .iref}

The 405 (Method Not Allowed) status code indicates that the method
received in the request-line is known by the origin server but not
supported by the [target resource](#target.resource){.xref}. The origin
server [MUST]{.bcp14} generate an [Allow](#field.allow){.xref} header
field in a 405 response containing a list of the target resource\'s
currently supported methods.[¶](#section-15.5.6-1){.pilcrow}

A 405 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.5.6-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.406}
::: {#section-15.5.7 .section}
#### [15.5.7.](#section-15.5.7){.section-number .selfRef} [406 Not Acceptable](#name-406-not-acceptable){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-406-not-acceptable}

[]{#iref-406-not-acceptable-status-c .iref}

The 406 (Not Acceptable) status code indicates that the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} does not have a current
representation that would be acceptable to the user agent, according to
the [proactive negotiation](#proactive.negotiation){.xref} header fields
received in the request ([Section 12.1](#proactive.negotiation){.xref}),
and the server is unwilling to supply a default
representation.[¶](#section-15.5.7-1){.pilcrow}

The server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate content containing a list of
available representation characteristics and corresponding resource
identifiers from which the user or user agent can choose the one most
appropriate. A user agent [MAY]{.bcp14} automatically select the most
appropriate choice from that list. However, this specification does not
define any standard for such automatic selection, as described in
[Section 15.4.1](#status.300){.xref}.[¶](#section-15.5.7-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.407}
::: {#section-15.5.8 .section}
#### [15.5.8.](#section-15.5.8){.section-number .selfRef} [407 Proxy Authentication Required](#name-407-proxy-authentication-re){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-407-proxy-authentication-re}

[]{#iref-407-proxy-authentication-re .iref}

The 407 (Proxy Authentication Required) status code is similar to [401
(Unauthorized)](#status.401){.xref}, but it indicates that the client
needs to authenticate itself in order to use a proxy for this request.
The proxy [MUST]{.bcp14} send a
[Proxy-Authenticate](#field.proxy-authenticate){.xref} header field
([Section 11.7.1](#field.proxy-authenticate){.xref}) containing a
challenge applicable to that proxy for the request. The client
[MAY]{.bcp14} repeat the request with a new or replaced
[Proxy-Authorization](#field.proxy-authorization){.xref} header field
([Section
11.7.2](#field.proxy-authorization){.xref}).[¶](#section-15.5.8-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.408}
::: {#section-15.5.9 .section}
#### [15.5.9.](#section-15.5.9){.section-number .selfRef} [408 Request Timeout](#name-408-request-timeout){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-408-request-timeout}

[]{#iref-408-request-timeout-status- .iref}

The 408 (Request Timeout) status code indicates that the server did not
receive a complete request message within the time that it was prepared
to wait.[¶](#section-15.5.9-1){.pilcrow}

If the client has an outstanding request in transit, it [MAY]{.bcp14}
repeat that request. If the current connection is not usable (e.g., as
it would be in HTTP/1.1 because request delimitation is lost), a new
connection will be used.[¶](#section-15.5.9-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.409}
::: {#section-15.5.10 .section}
#### [15.5.10.](#section-15.5.10){.section-number .selfRef} [409 Conflict](#name-409-conflict){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-409-conflict}

[]{#iref-409-conflict-status-code-43 .iref}

The 409 (Conflict) status code indicates that the request could not be
completed due to a conflict with the current state of the target
resource. This code is used in situations where the user might be able
to resolve the conflict and resubmit the request. The server
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} generate content that includes enough information for a
user to recognize the source of the
conflict.[¶](#section-15.5.10-1){.pilcrow}

Conflicts are most likely to occur in response to a PUT request. For
example, if versioning were being used and the representation being PUT
included changes to a resource that conflict with those made by an
earlier (third-party) request, the origin server might use a 409
response to indicate that it can\'t complete the request. In this case,
the response representation would likely contain information useful for
merging the differences based on the revision
history.[¶](#section-15.5.10-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.410}
::: {#section-15.5.11 .section}
#### [15.5.11.](#section-15.5.11){.section-number .selfRef} [410 Gone](#name-410-gone){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-410-gone}

[]{#iref-410-gone-status-code-434 .iref}

The 410 (Gone) status code indicates that access to the [target
resource](#target.resource){.xref} is no longer available at the origin
server and that this condition is likely to be permanent. If the origin
server does not know, or has no facility to determine, whether or not
the condition is permanent, the status code [404 (Not
Found)](#status.404){.xref} ought to be used
instead.[¶](#section-15.5.11-1){.pilcrow}

The 410 response is primarily intended to assist the task of web
maintenance by notifying the recipient that the resource is
intentionally unavailable and that the server owners desire that remote
links to that resource be removed. Such an event is common for
limited-time, promotional services and for resources belonging to
individuals no longer associated with the origin server\'s site. It is
not necessary to mark all permanently unavailable resources as \"gone\"
or to keep the mark for any length of time \-- that is left to the
discretion of the server owner.[¶](#section-15.5.11-2){.pilcrow}

A 410 response is heuristically cacheable; i.e., unless otherwise
indicated by the method definition or explicit cache controls (see
[Section
4.2.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc9111#section-4.2.2){.relref} of
\[[CACHING](#CACHING){.xref}\]).[¶](#section-15.5.11-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.411}
::: {#section-15.5.12 .section}
#### [15.5.12.](#section-15.5.12){.section-number .selfRef} [411 Length Required](#name-411-length-required){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-411-length-required}

[]{#iref-411-length-required-status- .iref}

The 411 (Length Required) status code indicates that the server refuses
to accept the request without a defined
[Content-Length](#field.content-length){.xref} ([Section
8.6](#field.content-length){.xref}). The client [MAY]{.bcp14} repeat the
request if it adds a valid Content-Length header field containing the
length of the request content.[¶](#section-15.5.12-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.412}
::: {#section-15.5.13 .section}
#### [15.5.13.](#section-15.5.13){.section-number .selfRef} [412 Precondition Failed](#name-412-precondition-failed){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-412-precondition-failed}

[]{#iref-412-precondition-failed-sta .iref}

The 412 (Precondition Failed) status code indicates that one or more
conditions given in the request header fields evaluated to false when
tested on the server ([Section 13](#conditional.requests){.xref}). This
response status code allows the client to place preconditions on the
current resource state (its current representations and metadata) and,
thus, prevent the request method from being applied if the target
resource is in an unexpected state.[¶](#section-15.5.13-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.413}
::: {#section-15.5.14 .section}
#### [15.5.14.](#section-15.5.14){.section-number .selfRef} [413 Content Too Large](#name-413-content-too-large){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-413-content-too-large}

[]{#iref-413-content-too-large-statu .iref}

The 413 (Content Too Large) status code indicates that the server is
refusing to process a request because the request content is larger than
the server is willing or able to process. The server [MAY]{.bcp14}
