([Section 4.2.2](#https.uri){.xref}).[¶](#section-17.16.1-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#auth.credentials.and.idle.clients}
::: {#section-17.16.2 .section}
#### [17.16.2.](#section-17.16.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Credentials and Idle Clients](#name-credentials-and-idle-client){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-credentials-and-idle-client}

Existing HTTP clients and user agents typically retain authentication
information indefinitely. HTTP does not provide a mechanism for the
origin server to direct clients to discard these cached credentials,
since the protocol has no awareness of how credentials are obtained or
managed by the user agent. The mechanisms for expiring or revoking
credentials can be specified as part of an authentication scheme
definition.[¶](#section-17.16.2-1){.pilcrow}

Circumstances under which credential caching can interfere with the
application\'s security model include but are not limited
to:[¶](#section-17.16.2-2){.pilcrow}

-   [Clients that have been idle for an extended period, following which
    the server might wish to cause the client to re-prompt the user for
    credentials.[¶](#section-17.16.2-3.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-17.16.2-3.1}
-   [Applications that include a session termination indication (such as
    a \"logout\" or \"commit\" button on a page) after which the server
    side of the application \"knows\" that there is no further reason
    for the client to retain the
    credentials.[¶](#section-17.16.2-3.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-17.16.2-3.2}

User agents that cache credentials are encouraged to provide a readily
accessible mechanism for discarding cached credentials under user
control.[¶](#section-17.16.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#protection.spaces}
::: {#section-17.16.3 .section}
#### [17.16.3.](#section-17.16.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Protection Spaces](#name-protection-spaces){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-protection-spaces}

Authentication schemes that solely rely on the \"realm\" mechanism for
establishing a protection space will expose credentials to all resources
on an origin server. Clients that have successfully made authenticated
requests with a resource can use the same authentication credentials for
other resources on the same origin server. This makes it possible for a
different resource to harvest authentication credentials for other
resources.[¶](#section-17.16.3-1){.pilcrow}

This is of particular concern when an origin server hosts resources for
multiple parties under the same origin ([Section
11.5](#protection.space){.xref}). Possible mitigation strategies include
restricting direct access to authentication credentials (i.e., not
making the content of the [Authorization](#field.authorization){.xref}
request header field available), and separating protection spaces by
using a different host name (or port number) for each
party.[¶](#section-17.16.3-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#security.auth.add.resp}
::: {#section-17.16.4 .section}
#### [17.16.4.](#section-17.16.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Additional Response Fields](#name-additional-response-fields){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-additional-response-fields}

Adding information to responses that are sent over an unencrypted
channel can affect security and privacy. The presence of the
[Authentication-Info](#field.authentication-info){.xref} and
[Proxy-Authentication-Info](#field.proxy-authentication-info){.xref}
header fields alone indicates that HTTP authentication is in use.
Additional information could be exposed by the contents of the
authentication-scheme specific parameters; this will have to be
considered in the definitions of these
schemes.[¶](#section-17.16.4-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#IANA.considerations}
::: {#section-18 .section}
## [18.](#section-18){.section-number .selfRef} [IANA Considerations](#name-iana-considerations){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-iana-considerations}

The change controller for the following registrations is: \"IETF
(iesg\@ietf.org) - Internet Engineering Task
Force\".[¶](#section-18-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#uri.scheme.registration}
::: {#section-18.1 .section}
### [18.1.](#section-18.1){.section-number .selfRef} [URI Scheme Registration](#name-uri-scheme-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-uri-scheme-registration}

IANA has updated the \"Uniform Resource Identifier (URI) Schemes\"
registry \[[BCP35](#BCP35){.xref}\] at
\<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/uri-schemes/>\> with the permanent
schemes listed in [Table 2](#uri.scheme.table){.xref} in [Section
4.2](#uri.schemes){.xref}.[¶](#section-18.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#method.registration}
::: {#section-18.2 .section}
### [18.2.](#section-18.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Method Registration](#name-method-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-method-registration}

IANA has updated the \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) Method
Registry\" at \<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/http-methods>\> with
the registration procedure of [Section 16.1.1](#method.registry){.xref}
and the method names summarized in the following
table.[¶](#section-18.2-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#iana.method.registration.table}
  Method    Safe   Idempotent   Section
  --------- ------ ------------ -------------------------------------
  CONNECT   no     no           [9.3.6](#CONNECT){.xref}
  DELETE    no     yes          [9.3.5](#DELETE){.xref}
  GET       yes    yes          [9.3.1](#GET){.xref}
  HEAD      yes    yes          [9.3.2](#HEAD){.xref}
  OPTIONS   yes    yes          [9.3.7](#OPTIONS){.xref}
  POST      no     no           [9.3.3](#POST){.xref}
  PUT       no     yes          [9.3.4](#PUT){.xref}
  TRACE     yes    yes          [9.3.8](#TRACE){.xref}
  \*        no     no           [18.2](#method.registration){.xref}

  : [Table 7](#table-7){.selfRef}
:::

[]{#iref-method-456 .iref} The method name \"\*\" is reserved because
using \"\*\" as a method name would conflict with its usage as a
wildcard in some fields (e.g.,
\"Access-Control-Request-Method\").[¶](#section-18.2-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status.code.registration}
::: {#section-18.3 .section}
### [18.3.](#section-18.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Status Code Registration](#name-status-code-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-status-code-registration}

IANA has updated the \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) Status Code
Registry\" at \<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/http-status-codes>\>
with the registration procedure of [Section
16.2.1](#status.code.registry){.xref} and the status code values
summarized in the following table.[¶](#section-18.3-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#iana.status.code.registration.table}
  Value   Description                     Section
  ------- ------------------------------- -------------------------------
  100     Continue                        [15.2.1](#status.100){.xref}
  101     Switching Protocols             [15.2.2](#status.101){.xref}
  200     OK                              [15.3.1](#status.200){.xref}
  201     Created                         [15.3.2](#status.201){.xref}
  202     Accepted                        [15.3.3](#status.202){.xref}
  203     Non-Authoritative Information   [15.3.4](#status.203){.xref}
  204     No Content                      [15.3.5](#status.204){.xref}
  205     Reset Content                   [15.3.6](#status.205){.xref}

  300     Multiple Choices                [15.4.1](#status.300){.xref}
  301     Moved Permanently               [15.4.2](#status.301){.xref}
  302     Found                           [15.4.3](#status.302){.xref}
  303     See Other                       [15.4.4](#status.303){.xref}
  304     Not Modified                    [15.4.5](#status.304){.xref}

  308     Permanent Redirect              [15.4.9](#status.308){.xref}
  400     Bad Request                     [15.5.1](#status.400){.xref}
  401     Unauthorized                    [15.5.2](#status.401){.xref}
  402     Payment Required                [15.5.3](#status.402){.xref}
  403     Forbidden                       [15.5.4](#status.403){.xref}
  404     Not Found                       [15.5.5](#status.404){.xref}
  405     Method Not Allowed              [15.5.6](#status.405){.xref}
  406     Not Acceptable                  [15.5.7](#status.406){.xref}
  407     Proxy Authentication Required   [15.5.8](#status.407){.xref}
  408     Request Timeout                 [15.5.9](#status.408){.xref}
  409     Conflict                        [15.5.10](#status.409){.xref}
  410     Gone                            [15.5.11](#status.410){.xref}
  411     Length Required                 [15.5.12](#status.411){.xref}
  412     Precondition Failed             [15.5.13](#status.412){.xref}
  413     Content Too Large               [15.5.14](#status.413){.xref}
  414     URI Too Long                    [15.5.15](#status.414){.xref}
  415     Unsupported Media Type          [15.5.16](#status.415){.xref}
  416     Range Not Satisfiable           [15.5.17](#status.416){.xref}
  417     Expectation Failed              [15.5.18](#status.417){.xref}
  418     (Unused)                        [15.5.19](#status.418){.xref}
  421     Misdirected Request             [15.5.20](#status.421){.xref}
  422     Unprocessable Content           [15.5.21](#status.422){.xref}
  426     Upgrade Required                [15.5.22](#status.426){.xref}
  500     Internal Server Error           [15.6.1](#status.500){.xref}
  501     Not Implemented                 [15.6.2](#status.501){.xref}
  502     Bad Gateway                     [15.6.3](#status.502){.xref}
  503     Service Unavailable             [15.6.4](#status.503){.xref}
  504     Gateway Timeout                 [15.6.5](#status.504){.xref}
  505     HTTP Version Not Supported      [15.6.6](#status.505){.xref}

  : [Table 8](#table-8){.selfRef}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#field.name.registration}
::: {#section-18.4 .section}
### [18.4.](#section-18.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Field Name Registration](#name-field-name-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-field-name-registration}

This specification updates the HTTP-related aspects of the existing
registration procedures for message header fields defined in
\[[RFC3864](#RFC3864){.xref}\]. It replaces the old procedures as they
relate to HTTP by defining a new registration procedure and moving HTTP
field definitions into a separate
registry.[¶](#section-18.4-1){.pilcrow}

IANA has created a new registry titled \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol
(HTTP) Field Name Registry\" as outlined in [Section
16.3.1](#fields.registry){.xref}.[¶](#section-18.4-2){.pilcrow}

IANA has moved all entries in the \"Permanent Message Header Field
Names\" and \"Provisional Message Header Field Names\" registries (see
\<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/message-headers/>\>) with the
protocol \'http\' to this registry and has applied the following
changes:[¶](#section-18.4-3){.pilcrow}

1.  [The \'Applicable Protocol\' field has been
    omitted.[¶](#section-18.4-4.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.4-4.1}
2.  [Entries that had a status of \'standard\', \'experimental\',
    \'reserved\', or \'informational\' have been made to have a status
    of
    \'permanent\'.[¶](#section-18.4-4.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.4-4.2}
3.  [Provisional entries without a status have been made to have a
    status of
    \'provisional\'.[¶](#section-18.4-4.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.4-4.3}
4.  [Permanent entries without a status (after confirmation that the
    registration document did not define one) have been made to have a
    status of \'provisional\'. The expert(s) can choose to update the
    entries\' status if there is evidence that another is more
    appropriate.[¶](#section-18.4-4.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.4-4.4}

IANA has annotated the \"Permanent Message Header Field Names\" and
\"Provisional Message Header Field Names\" registries with the following
note to indicate that HTTP field name registrations have
moved:[¶](#section-18.4-5){.pilcrow}

**Note**[¶](#section-18.4-6.1){.pilcrow}

HTTP field name registrations have been moved to
\[<https://www.iana.org/assignments/http-fields>\] per
\[RFC9110\].[¶](#section-18.4-6.2){.pilcrow}

IANA has updated the \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) Field Name
Registry\" with the field names listed in the following
table.[¶](#section-18.4-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#iana.header.registration.table}
  Field Name                  Status       Section                                             Comments
  --------------------------- ------------ --------------------------------------------------- ------------
  Accept                      permanent    [12.5.1](#field.accept){.xref}                      
  Accept-Charset              deprecated   [12.5.2](#field.accept-charset){.xref}              
  Accept-Encoding             permanent    [12.5.3](#field.accept-encoding){.xref}             
  Accept-Language             permanent    [12.5.4](#field.accept-language){.xref}             
  Accept-Ranges               permanent    [14.3](#field.accept-ranges){.xref}                 
  Allow                       permanent    [10.2.1](#field.allow){.xref}                       
  Authentication-Info         permanent    [11.6.3](#field.authentication-info){.xref}         
  Authorization               permanent    [11.6.2](#field.authorization){.xref}               
  Connection                  permanent    [7.6.1](#field.connection){.xref}                   
  Content-Encoding            permanent    [8.4](#field.content-encoding){.xref}               
  Content-Language            permanent    [8.5](#field.content-language){.xref}               
  Content-Length              permanent    [8.6](#field.content-length){.xref}                 
  Content-Location            permanent    [8.7](#field.content-location){.xref}               
  Content-Range               permanent    [14.4](#field.content-range){.xref}                 
  Content-Type                permanent    [8.3](#field.content-type){.xref}                   
  Date                        permanent    [6.6.1](#field.date){.xref}                         
  ETag                        permanent    [8.8.3](#field.etag){.xref}                         
  Expect                      permanent    [10.1.1](#field.expect){.xref}                      
  From                        permanent    [10.1.2](#field.from){.xref}                        
  Host                        permanent    [7.2](#field.host){.xref}                           
  If-Match                    permanent    [13.1.1](#field.if-match){.xref}                    
  If-Modified-Since           permanent    [13.1.3](#field.if-modified-since){.xref}           
  If-None-Match               permanent    [13.1.2](#field.if-none-match){.xref}               
  If-Range                    permanent    [13.1.5](#field.if-range){.xref}                    
  If-Unmodified-Since         permanent    [13.1.4](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref}         
  Last-Modified               permanent    [8.8.2](#field.last-modified){.xref}                
  Location                    permanent    [10.2.2](#field.location){.xref}                    
  Max-Forwards                permanent    [7.6.2](#field.max-forwards){.xref}                 
  Proxy-Authenticate          permanent    [11.7.1](#field.proxy-authenticate){.xref}          
  Proxy-Authentication-Info   permanent    [11.7.3](#field.proxy-authentication-info){.xref}   
  Proxy-Authorization         permanent    [11.7.2](#field.proxy-authorization){.xref}         
  Range                       permanent    [14.2](#field.range){.xref}                         
  Referer                     permanent    [10.1.3](#field.referer){.xref}                     
  Retry-After                 permanent    [10.2.3](#field.retry-after){.xref}                 
  Server                      permanent    [10.2.4](#field.server){.xref}                      
  TE                          permanent    [10.1.4](#field.te){.xref}                          
  Trailer                     permanent    [6.6.2](#field.trailer){.xref}                      
  Upgrade                     permanent    [7.8](#field.upgrade){.xref}                        
  User-Agent                  permanent    [10.1.5](#field.user-agent){.xref}                  
  Vary                        permanent    [12.5.5](#field.vary){.xref}                        
  Via                         permanent    [7.6.3](#field.via){.xref}                          
  WWW-Authenticate            permanent    [11.6.1](#field.www-authenticate){.xref}            
  \*                          permanent    [12.5.5](#field.vary){.xref}                        (reserved)

  : [Table 9](#table-9){.selfRef}
:::

::: {#field.asterisk}
[]{#iref-fields-457 .iref} The field name \"\*\" is reserved because
using that name as an HTTP header field might conflict with its special
semantics in the [Vary](#field.vary){.xref} header field ([Section
12.5.5](#field.vary){.xref}).[¶](#section-18.4-9){.pilcrow}
:::

[]{#iref-fields-content-md5-458 .iref}
[]{#iref-header-fields-content-md5-4 .iref}
[]{#iref-content-md5-header-field-46 .iref} IANA has updated the
\"Content-MD5\" entry in the new registry to have a status of
\'obsoleted\' with references to [Section
14.15](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc2616#section-14.15){.relref} of
\[[RFC2616](#RFC2616){.xref}\] (for the definition of the header field)
and [Appendix
B](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7231#appendix-B){.relref} of
\[[RFC7231](#RFC7231){.xref}\] (which removed the field definition from
the updated specification).[¶](#section-18.4-10){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-18.5 .section}
### [18.5.](#section-18.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Authentication Scheme Registration](#name-authentication-scheme-regist){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-authentication-scheme-regist}

IANA has updated the \"Hypertext Transfer Protocol (HTTP) Authentication
Scheme Registry\" at
\<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/http-authschemes>\> with the
registration procedure of [Section
16.4.1](#auth.scheme.registry){.xref}. No authentication schemes are
defined in this document.[¶](#section-18.5-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#content.coding.registration}
::: {#section-18.6 .section}
### [18.6.](#section-18.6){.section-number .selfRef} [Content Coding Registration](#name-content-coding-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-content-coding-registration}

IANA has updated the \"HTTP Content Coding Registry\" at
\<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/http-parameters/>\> with the
registration procedure of [Section
16.6.1](#content.coding.registry){.xref} and the content coding names
summarized in the table below.[¶](#section-18.6-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#iana.content.coding.registration.table}
  Name         Description                                                                                                                     Section
  ------------ ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- -----------------------------------------
  compress     UNIX \"compress\" data format \[[Welch](#Welch){.xref}\]                                                                        [8.4.1.1](#compress.coding){.xref}
  deflate      \"deflate\" compressed data (\[[RFC1951](#RFC1951){.xref}\]) inside the \"zlib\" data format (\[[RFC1950](#RFC1950){.xref}\])   [8.4.1.2](#deflate.coding){.xref}
  gzip         GZIP file format \[[RFC1952](#RFC1952){.xref}\]                                                                                 [8.4.1.3](#gzip.coding){.xref}
  identity     Reserved                                                                                                                        [12.5.3](#field.accept-encoding){.xref}
  x-compress   Deprecated (alias for compress)                                                                                                 [8.4.1.1](#compress.coding){.xref}
  x-gzip       Deprecated (alias for gzip)                                                                                                     [8.4.1.3](#gzip.coding){.xref}

  : [Table 10](#table-10){.selfRef}
:::

::: {#port.reg}
::: {#section-18.9 .section}
### [18.9.](#section-18.9){.section-number .selfRef} [Port Registration](#name-port-registration){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-port-registration}

IANA has updated the \"Service Name and Transport Protocol Port Number
Registry\" at
\<<https://www.iana.org/assignments/service-names-port-numbers/>\> for
the services on ports 80 and 443 that use UDP or TCP
to:[¶](#section-18.9-1){.pilcrow}

1.  [use this document as \"Reference\",
    and[¶](#section-18.9-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.9-2.1}
2.  [when currently unspecified, set \"Assignee\" to \"IESG\" and
    \"Contact\" to
    \"IETF_Chair\".[¶](#section-18.9-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-18.9-2.2}
:::

  Name   Description                   Expected Version Tokens           Section
  ------ ----------------------------- --------------------------------- ---------------------------------
  HTTP   Hypertext Transfer Protocol   any DIGIT.DIGIT (e.g., \"2.0\")   [2.5](#protocol.version){.xref}

::: {#collected.abnf}
::: {#appendix-A .section}
## [Appendix A.](#appendix-A){.section-number .selfRef} [Collected ABNF](#name-collected-abnf){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-collected-abnf}

In the collected ABNF below, list rules are expanded per [Section
5.6.1](#abnf.extension){.xref}.[¶](#appendix-A-1){.pilcrow}

::: {#appendix-A-2}
``` {.breakable .lang-abnf .sourcecode}
Accept = [ ( media-range [ weight ] ) *( OWS "," OWS ( media-range [
 weight ] ) ) ]
Accept-Charset = [ ( ( token / "*" ) [ weight ] ) *( OWS "," OWS ( (
 token / "*" ) [ weight ] ) ) ]
Accept-Encoding = [ ( codings [ weight ] ) *( OWS "," OWS ( codings [
 weight ] ) ) ]
Accept-Language = [ ( language-range [ weight ] ) *( OWS "," OWS (
 language-range [ weight ] ) ) ]
Accept-Ranges = acceptable-ranges
Allow = [ method *( OWS "," OWS method ) ]
Authentication-Info = [ auth-param *( OWS "," OWS auth-param ) ]
Authorization = credentials

BWS = OWS

Connection = [ connection-option *( OWS "," OWS connection-option )
 ]
Content-Encoding = [ content-coding *( OWS "," OWS content-coding )
 ]
Content-Language = [ language-tag *( OWS "," OWS language-tag ) ]
Content-Length = 1*DIGIT
Content-Location = absolute-URI / partial-URI
Content-Range = range-unit SP ( range-resp / unsatisfied-range )
Content-Type = media-type

Date = HTTP-date

ETag = entity-tag
Expect = [ expectation *( OWS "," OWS expectation ) ]

From = mailbox

GMT = %x47.4D.54 ; GMT

HTTP-date = IMF-fixdate / obs-date
Host = uri-host [ ":" port ]

IMF-fixdate = day-name "," SP date1 SP time-of-day SP GMT
If-Match = "*" / [ entity-tag *( OWS "," OWS entity-tag ) ]
If-Modified-Since = HTTP-date
If-None-Match = "*" / [ entity-tag *( OWS "," OWS entity-tag ) ]
If-Range = entity-tag / HTTP-date
If-Unmodified-Since = HTTP-date

Last-Modified = HTTP-date
Location = URI-reference

Max-Forwards = 1*DIGIT

OWS = *( SP / HTAB )

Proxy-Authenticate = [ challenge *( OWS "," OWS challenge ) ]
Proxy-Authentication-Info = [ auth-param *( OWS "," OWS auth-param )
 ]
Proxy-Authorization = credentials

RWS = 1*( SP / HTAB )
Range = ranges-specifier
Referer = absolute-URI / partial-URI
Retry-After = HTTP-date / delay-seconds

Server = product *( RWS ( product / comment ) )

TE = [ t-codings *( OWS "," OWS t-codings ) ]
Trailer = [ field-name *( OWS "," OWS field-name ) ]

URI-reference = <URI-reference, see [URI], Section 4.1>
Upgrade = [ protocol *( OWS "," OWS protocol ) ]
User-Agent = product *( RWS ( product / comment ) )

Vary = [ ( "*" / field-name ) *( OWS "," OWS ( "*" / field-name ) )
 ]
Via = [ ( received-protocol RWS received-by [ RWS comment ] ) *( OWS
 "," OWS ( received-protocol RWS received-by [ RWS comment ] ) ) ]

WWW-Authenticate = [ challenge *( OWS "," OWS challenge ) ]

absolute-URI = <absolute-URI, see [URI], Section 4.3>
absolute-path = 1*( "/" segment )
acceptable-ranges = range-unit *( OWS "," OWS range-unit )
asctime-date = day-name SP date3 SP time-of-day SP year
auth-param = token BWS "=" BWS ( token / quoted-string )
auth-scheme = token
authority = <authority, see [URI], Section 3.2>

challenge = auth-scheme [ 1*SP ( token68 / [ auth-param *( OWS ","
 OWS auth-param ) ] ) ]
codings = content-coding / "identity" / "*"
comment = "(" *( ctext / quoted-pair / comment ) ")"
complete-length = 1*DIGIT
connection-option = token
content-coding = token
credentials = auth-scheme [ 1*SP ( token68 / [ auth-param *( OWS ","
 OWS auth-param ) ] ) ]
ctext = HTAB / SP / %x21-27 ; '!'-'''
 / %x2A-5B ; '*'-'['
 / %x5D-7E ; ']'-'~'
 / obs-text

date1 = day SP month SP year
date2 = day "-" month "-" 2DIGIT
date3 = month SP ( 2DIGIT / ( SP DIGIT ) )
day = 2DIGIT
day-name = %x4D.6F.6E ; Mon
 / %x54.75.65 ; Tue
 / %x57.65.64 ; Wed
 / %x54.68.75 ; Thu
 / %x46.72.69 ; Fri
 / %x53.61.74 ; Sat
 / %x53.75.6E ; Sun
day-name-l = %x4D.6F.6E.64.61.79 ; Monday
 / %x54.75.65.73.64.61.79 ; Tuesday
 / %x57.65.64.6E.65.73.64.61.79 ; Wednesday
 / %x54.68.75.72.73.64.61.79 ; Thursday
 / %x46.72.69.64.61.79 ; Friday
 / %x53.61.74.75.72.64.61.79 ; Saturday
 / %x53.75.6E.64.61.79 ; Sunday
delay-seconds = 1*DIGIT

entity-tag = [ weak ] opaque-tag
etagc = "!" / %x23-7E ; '#'-'~'
 / obs-text
expectation = token [ "=" ( token / quoted-string ) parameters ]

field-content = field-vchar [ 1*( SP / HTAB / field-vchar )
 field-vchar ]
field-name = token
field-value = *field-content
field-vchar = VCHAR / obs-text
first-pos = 1*DIGIT

hour = 2DIGIT
http-URI = "http://" authority path-abempty [ "?" query ]
https-URI = "https://" authority path-abempty [ "?" query ]

incl-range = first-pos "-" last-pos
int-range = first-pos "-" [ last-pos ]

language-range = <language-range, see [RFC4647], Section 2.1>
language-tag = <Language-Tag, see [RFC5646], Section 2.1>
last-pos = 1*DIGIT

mailbox = <mailbox, see [RFC5322], Section 3.4>
media-range = ( "*/*" / ( type "/*" ) / ( type "/" subtype ) )
 parameters
media-type = type "/" subtype parameters
method = token
minute = 2DIGIT
month = %x4A.61.6E ; Jan
 / %x46.65.62 ; Feb
 / %x4D.61.72 ; Mar
 / %x41.70.72 ; Apr
 / %x4D.61.79 ; May
 / %x4A.75.6E ; Jun
 / %x4A.75.6C ; Jul
 / %x41.75.67 ; Aug
 / %x53.65.70 ; Sep
 / %x4F.63.74 ; Oct
 / %x4E.6F.76 ; Nov
 / %x44.65.63 ; Dec

obs-date = rfc850-date / asctime-date
obs-text = %x80-FF
opaque-tag = DQUOTE *etagc DQUOTE
other-range = 1*( %x21-2B ; '!'-'+'
 / %x2D-7E ; '-'-'~'
 )

parameter = parameter-name "=" parameter-value
parameter-name = token
parameter-value = ( token / quoted-string )
parameters = *( OWS ";" OWS [ parameter ] )
partial-URI = relative-part [ "?" query ]
path-abempty = <path-abempty, see [URI], Section 3.3>
port = <port, see [URI], Section 3.2.3>
product = token [ "/" product-version ]
product-version = token
protocol = protocol-name [ "/" protocol-version ]
protocol-name = token
protocol-version = token
pseudonym = token

qdtext = HTAB / SP / "!" / %x23-5B ; '#'-'['
 / %x5D-7E ; ']'-'~'
 / obs-text
query = <query, see [URI], Section 3.4>
quoted-pair = "\" ( HTAB / SP / VCHAR / obs-text )
quoted-string = DQUOTE *( qdtext / quoted-pair ) DQUOTE
qvalue = ( "0" [ "." *3DIGIT ] ) / ( "1" [ "." *3"0" ] )

range-resp = incl-range "/" ( complete-length / "*" )
range-set = range-spec *( OWS "," OWS range-spec )
range-spec = int-range / suffix-range / other-range
range-unit = token
ranges-specifier = range-unit "=" range-set
received-by = pseudonym [ ":" port ]
received-protocol = [ protocol-name "/" ] protocol-version
relative-part = <relative-part, see [URI], Section 4.2>
rfc850-date = day-name-l "," SP date2 SP time-of-day SP GMT

second = 2DIGIT
segment = <segment, see [URI], Section 3.3>
subtype = token
suffix-length = 1*DIGIT
suffix-range = "-" suffix-length

t-codings = "trailers" / ( transfer-coding [ weight ] )
tchar = "!" / "#" / "$" / "%" / "&" / "'" / "*" / "+" / "-" / "." /
 "^" / "_" / "`" / "|" / "~" / DIGIT / ALPHA
time-of-day = hour ":" minute ":" second
token = 1*tchar
token68 = 1*( ALPHA / DIGIT / "-" / "." / "_" / "~" / "+" / "/" )
 *"="
transfer-coding = token *( OWS ";" OWS transfer-parameter )
transfer-parameter = token BWS "=" BWS ( token / quoted-string )
type = token

unsatisfied-range = "*/" complete-length
uri-host = <host, see [URI], Section 3.2.2>

weak = %x57.2F ; W/
weight = OWS ";" OWS "q=" qvalue

year = 4DIGIT
```

[¶](#appendix-A-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.previous.rfcs}
::: {#appendix-B .section}
## [Appendix B.](#appendix-B){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from Previous RFCs](#name-changes-from-previous-rfcs){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-previous-rfcs}

::: {#changes.from.rfc.2818}
::: {#appendix-B.1 .section}
### [B.1.](#appendix-B.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 2818](#name-changes-from-rfc-2818){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-2818}

None.[¶](#appendix-B.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.rfc.7230}
::: {#appendix-B.2 .section}
### [B.2.](#appendix-B.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 7230](#name-changes-from-rfc-7230){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-7230}

The sections introducing HTTP\'s design goals, history, architecture,
conformance criteria, protocol versioning, URIs, message routing, and
header fields have been moved here.[¶](#appendix-B.2-1){.pilcrow}

The requirement on semantic conformance has been replaced with
permission to ignore or work around implementation-specific failures.
([Section
2.2](#requirements.notation){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-2){.pilcrow}

The description of an origin and authoritative access to origin servers
has been extended for both \"http\" and \"https\" URIs to account for
alternative services and secured connections that are not necessarily
based on TCP. (Sections [4.2.1](#http.uri){.xref},
[4.2.2](#https.uri){.xref}, [4.3.1](#origin){.xref}, and
[7.3.3](#routing.origin){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-3){.pilcrow}

Explicit requirements have been added to check the target URI scheme\'s
semantics and reject requests that don\'t meet any associated
requirements. ([Section
7.4](#routing.reject){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-4){.pilcrow}

Parameters in media type, media range, and expectation can be empty via
one or more trailing semicolons. ([Section
5.6.6](#parameter){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-5){.pilcrow}

\"Field value\" now refers to the value after multiple field lines are
combined with commas \-- by far the most common use. To refer to a
single header line\'s value, use \"field line value\". ([Section
6.3](#header.fields){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-6){.pilcrow}

Trailer field semantics now transcend the specifics of chunked transfer
coding. The use of trailer fields has been further limited to allow
generation as a trailer field only when the sender knows the field
defines that usage and to allow merging into the header section only if
the recipient knows the corresponding field definition permits and
defines how to merge. In all other cases, implementations are encouraged
either to store the trailer fields separately or to discard them instead
of merging. ([Section
6.5.1](#trailers.limitations){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-7){.pilcrow}

The priority of the absolute form of the request URI over the Host
header field by origin servers has been made explicit to align with
proxy handling. ([Section
7.2](#field.host){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-8){.pilcrow}

The grammar definition for the Via field\'s \"received-by\" was expanded
in RFC 7230 due to changes in the URI grammar for host
\[[URI](#URI){.xref}\] that are not desirable for Via. For simplicity,
we have removed uri-host from the received-by production because it can
be encompassed by the existing grammar for pseudonym. In particular,
this change removed comma from the allowed set of characters for a host
name in received-by. ([Section
7.6.3](#field.via){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.2-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.rfc.7231}
::: {#appendix-B.3 .section}
### [B.3.](#appendix-B.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 7231](#name-changes-from-rfc-7231){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-7231}

Minimum URI lengths to be supported by implementations are now
recommended. ([Section
4.1](#uri.references){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-1){.pilcrow}

The following have been clarified: CR and NUL in field values are to be
rejected or mapped to SP, and leading and trailing whitespace needs to
be stripped from field values before they are consumed. ([Section
5.5](#fields.values){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-2){.pilcrow}

Parameters in media type, media range, and expectation can be empty via
one or more trailing semicolons. ([Section
5.6.6](#parameter){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-3){.pilcrow}

An abstract data type for HTTP messages has been introduced to define
the components of a message and their semantics as an abstraction across
multiple HTTP versions, rather than in terms of the specific syntax form
of HTTP/1.1 in \[[HTTP/1.1](#HTTP11){.xref}\], and reflect the contents
after the message is parsed. This makes it easier to distinguish between
requirements on the content (what is conveyed) versus requirements on
the messaging syntax (how it is conveyed) and avoids baking limitations
of early protocol versions into the future of HTTP. ([Section
6](#message.abstraction){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-4){.pilcrow}

The terms \"payload\" and \"payload body\" have been replaced with
\"content\", to better align with its usage elsewhere (e.g., in field
names) and to avoid confusion with frame payloads in HTTP/2 and HTTP/3.
([Section 6.4](#content){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-5){.pilcrow}

The term \"effective request URI\" has been replaced with \"target
URI\". ([Section
7.1](#target.resource){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-6){.pilcrow}

Restrictions on client retries have been loosened to reflect
implementation behavior. ([Section
9.2.2](#idempotent.methods){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-7){.pilcrow}

The fact that request bodies on GET, HEAD, and DELETE are not
interoperable has been clarified. (Sections [9.3.1](#GET){.xref},
[9.3.2](#HEAD){.xref}, and
[9.3.5](#DELETE){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-8){.pilcrow}

The use of the [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header field
([Section 14.4](#field.content-range){.xref}) as a request modifier on
PUT is allowed. ([Section
9.3.4](#PUT){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-9){.pilcrow}

A superfluous requirement about setting
[Content-Length](#field.content-length){.xref} has been removed from the
description of the OPTIONS method. ([Section
9.3.7](#OPTIONS){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-10){.pilcrow}

The normative requirement to use the \"message/http\" media type in
TRACE responses has been removed. ([Section
9.3.8](#TRACE){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-11){.pilcrow}

List-based grammar for [Expect](#field.expect){.xref} has been restored
for compatibility with RFC 2616. ([Section
10.1.1](#field.expect){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-12){.pilcrow}

[Accept](#field.accept){.xref} and
[Accept-Encoding](#field.accept-encoding){.xref} are allowed in response
messages; the latter was introduced by \[[RFC7694](#RFC7694){.xref}\].
([Section
12.3](#request.content.negotiation){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-13){.pilcrow}

\"Accept Parameters\" (accept-params and accept-ext ABNF production)
have been removed from the definition of the Accept field. ([Section
12.5.1](#field.accept){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-14){.pilcrow}

The Accept-Charset field is now deprecated. ([Section
12.5.2](#field.accept-charset){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-15){.pilcrow}

The semantics of \"\*\" in the [Vary](#field.vary){.xref} header field
when other values are present was clarified. ([Section
12.5.5](#field.vary){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-16){.pilcrow}

Range units are compared in a case-insensitive fashion. ([Section
14.1](#range.units){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-17){.pilcrow}

The use of the Accept-Ranges field is not restricted to origin servers.
([Section
14.3](#field.accept-ranges){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-18){.pilcrow}

The process of creating a redirected request has been clarified.
([Section 15.4](#status.3xx){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-19){.pilcrow}

Status code 308 (previously defined in \[[RFC7538](#RFC7538){.xref}\])
has been added so that it\'s defined closer to status codes 301, 302,
and 307. ([Section
15.4.9](#status.308){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-20){.pilcrow}

Status code 421 (previously defined in [Section
9.1.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc7540#section-9.1.2){.relref} of
\[[RFC7540](#RFC7540){.xref}\]) has been added because of its general
applicability. 421 is no longer defined as heuristically cacheable since
the response is specific to the connection (not the target resource).
([Section 15.5.20](#status.421){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-21){.pilcrow}

Status code 422 (previously defined in [Section
11.2](https://www.rfc-editor.org/rfc/rfc4918#section-11.2){.relref} of
\[[WEBDAV](#WEBDAV){.xref}\]) has been added because of its general
applicability. ([Section
15.5.21](#status.422){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.3-22){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.rfc.7232}
::: {#appendix-B.4 .section}
### [B.4.](#appendix-B.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 7232](#name-changes-from-rfc-7232){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-7232}

Previous revisions of HTTP imposed an arbitrary 60-second limit on the
determination of whether Last-Modified was a strong validator to guard
against the possibility that the Date and Last-Modified values are
generated from different clocks or at somewhat different times during
the preparation of the response. This specification has relaxed that to
allow reasonable discretion. ([Section
8.8.2.2](#lastmod.comparison){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.4-1){.pilcrow}

An edge-case requirement on If-Match and If-Unmodified-Since has been
removed that required a validator not to be sent in a 2xx response if
validation fails because the change request has already been applied.
(Sections [13.1.1](#field.if-match){.xref} and
[13.1.4](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.4-2){.pilcrow}

The fact that If-Unmodified-Since does not apply to a resource without a
concept of modification time has been clarified. ([Section
13.1.4](#field.if-unmodified-since){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.4-3){.pilcrow}

Preconditions can now be evaluated before the request content is
processed rather than waiting until the response would otherwise be
successful. ([Section
13.2](#evaluation){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.4-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.rfc.7233}
::: {#appendix-B.5 .section}
### [B.5.](#appendix-B.5){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 7233](#name-changes-from-rfc-7233){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-7233}

Refactored the range-unit and ranges-specifier grammars to simplify and
reduce artificial distinctions between bytes and other (extension) range
units, removing the overlapping grammar of other-range-unit by defining
range units generically as a token and placing extensions within the
scope of a range-spec (other-range). This disambiguates the role of list
syntax (commas) in all range sets, including extension range units, for
indicating a range-set of more than one range. Moving the extension
grammar into range specifiers also allows protocol specific to byte
ranges to be specified separately.[¶](#appendix-B.5-1){.pilcrow}

It is now possible to define Range handling on extension methods.
([Section 14.2](#field.range){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.5-2){.pilcrow}

Described use of the [Content-Range](#field.content-range){.xref} header
field ([Section 14.4](#field.content-range){.xref}) as a request
modifier to perform a partial PUT. ([Section
14.5](#partial.PUT){.xref})[¶](#appendix-B.5-3){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changes.from.rfc.7235}
::: {#appendix-B.6 .section}

None.[¶](#appendix-B.6-1){.pilcrow}
:::

### [B.9.](#appendix-B.9){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 7694](#name-changes-from-rfc-7694){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-7694}

This specification includes the extension defined in
\[[RFC7694](#RFC7694){.xref}\] but leaves out examples and deployment
considerations.[¶](#appendix-B.9-1){.pilcrow}
